2:21:1077:0:14:72:159:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Unequal Bequests
2:22:1093:14:14:72:370:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Marco Francesconi, Robert A. Pollak, and Domenico Tabasso
2:23:1150:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:NBER Working Paper No. 21692

2:26:1209:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:27:1217:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Using data from the Health and Retirement Study (HRS), we make two contributions to the literature
2:28:1315:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:on end-of-life transfers. First, we show that unequal bequests are much more common than generally
2:29:1413:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:recognized, with one-third of parents with wills planning to divide their estates unequally among their
2:30:1516:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:children. These plans for unequal division are particularly concentrated in complex families, which
2:31:1615:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:are of two types: families with stepchildren and families with genetic children with whom the parent
2:32:1715:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:has had no contact, e.g., children from previous marriages. We find that in complex families past and
2:33:1816:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:current contact between parents and children reduces or eliminates unequal bequests. Second, although
2:34:1917:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:the literature focuses on the bequest intentions of parents who have made wills, we find that many
2:35:2015:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:older Americans have not made wills. Although the probability of having a will increases with age,
2:36:2113:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:30 percent of HRS respondents aged 70 and over have no wills. Of HRS respondents who died between
2:37:2210:14:14:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:1995 and 2010, 38 percent died without wills. Thus, focusing exclusively on the bequest intentions
2:38:2308:14:14:72:539:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:of parents who have made wills may provide an incomplete and misleading picture of end-of-life
2:39:2402:14:42:72:116:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:transfers.
2:40:2412:42:14:72:164:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Marco Francesconi
2:41:2429:14:14:72:167:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:University of Essex
2:42:2448:14:14:72:173:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Colchester CO4 3SQ
2:43:2466:14:14:72:153:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:United Kingdom
2:44:2480:14:14:72:112:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and IZA
2:45:2487:14:28:72:172:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:mfranc@essex.ac.uk
2:46:2505:28:14:72:153:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Robert A. Pollak
2:47:2521:14:14:72:242:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Washington University in St. Louis
2:48:2555:14:14:72:158:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Arts and Sciences
2:49:2572:14:14:72:213:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and the Olin Business School
2:50:2600:14:14:72:161:224:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Campus Box 1133
2:51:2615:14:14:72:161:210:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:1 Brookings Drive
2:52:2632:14:14:72:205:196:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:St. Louis, MO  63130-4899
2:53:2657:14:14:72:112:182:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and IZA
2:54:2664:14:14:72:147:168:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and also NBER
2:55:2677:14:0:72:159:154:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:pollak@wustl.edu
2:56:2693:0:14:306:398:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:Domenico Tabasso
2:57:2709:14:14:306:409:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:University of Geneva
2:58:2729:14:14:306:439:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:and NCCR LIVES and IZA
2:59:2751:14:250:306:444:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:domenico.tabasso@unige.ch
2:60:2776:250:14:72:304:86:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:A Supplementary online material is available at:
2:61:2824:14:0:72:465:72:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:https://sites.google.com/site/domtabasso/appendix-material-for- unequal-bequests
3:62:2904:0:26:70:179:759:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1.  Introduction
3:63:2920:26:18:70:524:733:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In this paper we shed new light on bequest behavior using a large and nationally rep-
3:64:3005:18:18:70:524:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:resentative  US  sample  drawn  from  the  Health  and  Retirement  Study  (HRS)  over  the
3:65:3096:18:18:70:524:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period 1995–2010.  A distinguishing feature of our work is its focus on complex families,
3:66:3185:18:18:70:524:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in particular on parents with stepchildren and parents with genetic children with whom
3:67:3271:18:18:70:524:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they have limited or no contact (e.g., children from previous marriages).  We complement
3:68:3359:18:19:70:524:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our analysis of the bequest intentions of parents with wills by examining actual bequests
3:69:3448:19:18:70:524:624:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using reports about the disposition of the estates of HRS respondents who died between
3:70:3534:18:18:70:524:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one HRS wave and the next.  We find that unequal bequests (both intended and actual)
3:71:3618:18:18:70:524:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  much  more  prevalent  than  previously  documented,  with  one-third  of  parents  with
3:72:3711:18:18:70:524:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wills planning to distribute their estates unequally.  Unequal intended bequests are most
3:73:3800:18:18:70:524:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:common in complex families, but contact between parents and children reduces or elimi-
3:74:3886:18:18:70:524:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nates unequal bequests.  Finally, we find that a substantial fraction of older parents report
3:75:3979:18:18:70:507:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:having no wills and a substantial fraction of HRS respondents who died had no wills.
3:76:4063:18:18:88:524:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Empirical research has long established that a substantial majority of parents divide,
3:77:4149:18:18:70:524:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or intend to divide, their estates equally among their children (Menchik 1980; Wilhelm
3:78:4235:18:18:70:524:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1996;  McGarry  1999;  Cox  2003;  Light  and  McGarry  2004;  Behrman  and  Rosenzweig
3:79:4322:18:18:70:524:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2004).  Despite the fact that earlier economic models predicted unequal bequests (e.g.,
3:80:4409:18:18:70:524:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Becker 1974; Bernheim, Shleifer, and Summers 1985; Cox 1987), more recent studies have
3:81:4495:18:18:70:524:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:developed theories that attempt to rationalize the prevalence of equal bequests, sometimes
3:82:4585:18:18:70:524:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also attempting to explain why parents treat their children unequally with respect to inter
3:83:4676:18:18:70:524:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vivos transfers but equally with respect to bequests (e.g., Andreoni 1989; Bernheim and
3:84:4763:18:18:70:154:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Severinov 2003).
3:85:4779:18:19:88:524:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The proportion of American parents aged 50 and over who reported having wills,1in
3:86:4860:19:18:70:524:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which their children were treated unequally more than doubled between 1995 and 2010,
3:87:4944:18:18:70:524:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rising from 16 percent to almost 35 percent (Figure 1).2This upward trend, which holds
3:88:5030:18:18:70:523:281:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:for both mothers and fathers, is not simply driven by the ageing of the HRS respondents.3
3:89:5119:18:18:70:524:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A similar increase can be observed across several cohorts of Americans born since 1890
3:90:5205:18:18:70:524:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Figure 2).  Younger cohorts (i.e., those born in 1960 or after) are substantially more likely
3:91:5299:18:18:70:524:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to intend unequal bequests, with the sharpest increases occurring among individuals who
3:92:5386:18:18:70:523:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are no longer married:  widows, widowers, and divorced individuals (Figure 3).4Bequests,
3:93:5474:18:16:84:524:191:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:1We focus on the bequest intentions of parents with wills because most of the information on bequest
3:94:5574:16:12:70:524:175:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:intentions collected by HRS is from parents who report that they have wills.  See the data description in
3:95:5679:12:8:70:136:163:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:subsection 3.B.
3:96:5694:8:16:84:524:155:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:2Throughout the paper, stepchildren are counted as “children”. Moreover, although the legal definition
3:97:5796:16:12:70:524:139:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of stepchildren is narrow (i.e., a stepchild is the child of a spouse), we use this term broadly, to include
3:98:5904:12:8:70:448:127:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the children of a cohabiting partner as well as the children of a legally married spouse.
3:99:5993:8:16:84:524:119:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:3Between 1998 and 2010 the average age of the HRS sample increased only by four years.  This is due
3:100:6092:16:12:70:524:103:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:to a number of factors, including attrition, death of older respondents and, since 2004, the introduction
3:101:6197:12:8:70:260:91:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of new cohorts of individuals aged 51 to 56.
3:102:6241:8:0:84:460:83:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:4HRS data do not allow us to distinguish between cohabitors and married individuals.
4:103:6326:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:therefore, bear a strong relationship to demographics:  as demographics are changing so
4:104:6413:18:19:70:136:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are bequests.
4:105:6426:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since the middle of the 1990s the fraction of parents reporting unequal bequest inten-
4:106:6512:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions has consistently been 30–35 percentage points higher among parents with stepchil-
4:107:6599:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren than among those with genetic children only (Figure 4).  Comparing parents who
4:108:6682:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have had no contact with at least one of their genetic children with parents who have had
4:109:6771:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at least some contact with all of their genetic children,  we find the no-contact parents
4:110:6860:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about 35–45 percentage points less likely to intend equal bequests.5The trends in unequal
4:111:6949:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequest intentions among parents without contact with their children is the same as the
4:112:7036:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trend observed among parents with stepchildren.  As the proportion of complex families
4:113:7122:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has  risen  in  the  last  twenty  years,  so  has  the  proportion  of  parents  who  plan  unequal
4:114:7222:18:18:70:117:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequests.
4:115:7231:18:18:88:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When  individuals  die  without  a  valid  will,  the  intestacy  laws  of  their  state  provide
4:116:7328:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the default allocation,  dividing the decedent’s estate between the surviving spouse and
4:117:7416:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the children.6After providing an often very substantial share for the surviving spouse,
4:118:7503:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intestacy  laws  divide  the  remainder  equally  among  the  decedent’s  genetic  and  legally
4:119:7598:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adopted  children.   Unlike  surviving  spouses,  under  intestacy  laws  surviving  cohabiting
4:120:7693:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:partners inherit nothing. And, unlike genetic and legally adopted children, under intestacy
4:121:7784:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:laws  stepchildren  inherit  nothing  (Fried  1992;  Brashier  2004;  Friedman  2009;  Reid,  de
4:122:7880:19:18:70:229:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Waal, and Zimmermann 2011).
4:123:7907:18:18:88:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since 1998 the average fraction of HRS respondents without a will has been around 42
4:124:7991:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent (Figure 5).7Among respondents with stepchildren the average fraction without
4:125:8075:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wills is somewhat greater (49 percent),  and it is even greater among parents who have
4:126:8161:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no contact with their genetic children (58 percent).  Parents aged less than 70 are much
4:127:8249:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less likely to have wills, perhaps because writing a will is not yet salient for them, but a
4:128:8341:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:staggering 30 percent of parents aged 70 and over report not having wills.  The data also
4:129:8430:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reveal a slight education gradient (not shown):  HRS respondents with university degrees
4:130:8518:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or higher qualifications are more likely to have a will as opposed to their less educated
4:131:8607:18:18:70:137:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:counterparts.
4:132:8620:18:18:88:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Standard economic models ignore complex families.  The (usually implicit) assumption
4:133:8704:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is that all children are born to a married couple who remain married to each other.  When
4:134:8793:18:19:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one  spouse  dies,  the  surviving  spouse  is  (usually  implicitly)  assumed  not  to  remarry.
4:135:8890:19:15:84:524:180:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:5In 1995 the HRS did not ask the question on parent-child contact, while in 2010 the question was
4:136:8987:15:12:70:524:165:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:asked only to a small fraction of respondents.  For these reasons we do not show those two years in Figure
4:137:9093:12:9:70:78:153:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:4.
4:138:9095:9:15:84:524:144:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:6As Rosenbury (2005) shows, there are important differences in intestacy laws across states, but we
4:139:9194:15:8:70:282:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:focus on features that are common across states.
4:140:9242:8:16:84:524:121:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:7This figure starts in 1998 because the 1995 HRS wave oversampled older people (with an average age
4:141:9341:16:12:70:524:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of 78 years), while the 1996 wave oversampled younger individuals, whose average age is 59 years.  From
4:142:9444:12:12:70:524:93:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:1998 onwards, the study comprised both subsamples, and in that year individuals were on average aged
4:143:9544:12:0:70:83:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:67.
5:144:9548:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Little  is  said  about  divorce,  remarriage  or  repartnering  and  even  less  about  multiple
5:145:9645:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:partner fertility.8By ignoring divorce,  repartnering,  or remarriage,  canonical economic
5:146:9735:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models fail to recognize the increased complexity of the family (Bumpass and Lu 2000;
5:147:9820:18:18:70:394:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stevenson and Wolfers 2007; Lundberg and Pollak 2014, 2015).
5:148:9880:18:18:88:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In addition to presenting a representative picture of contemporary end-of-life transfers,
5:149:9969:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we make two contributions to the literature.  First, we show that unequal bequests are
5:150:10055:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:much  more  common  than  generally  recognized.   Unequal  bequests  are  concentrated  in
5:151:10146:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complex families, that is, families in which parents have stepchildren and families with
5:152:10234:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic children with whom the parent has had no contact (e.g., children from previous
5:153:10320:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marriages).  Parents with stepchildren are much less likely to include all children in their
5:154:10412:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wills  than  parents  without  stepchildren,  and  parents  with  stepchildren  who  have  wills
5:155:10508:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are substantially less likely to plan equal bequests.  Similarly, parents who have had no
5:156:10597:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact with one or more of their genetic children are less likely to include all of their
5:157:10687:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children in their wills.  When all children are included in the parent’s will, we find that
5:158:10778:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents with no-contact children are less likely to plan equal bequests.  The likelihood of
5:159:10869:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unequal bequests, however, is reduced and often entirely eliminated by longer coresidence
5:160:10958:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of stepparents and stepchildren.  We interpret this finding as reflecting the accumulation
5:161:11048:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of family-specific capital (e.g., trust and affection) that triggers norms of equal treatment.
5:162:11142:18:19:88:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our second contribution to the literature on end-of-life transfers shifts the focus from
5:163:11230:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individuals with wills to those who die intestate (i.e., without wills).  We find that many
5:164:11321:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:older  Americans  do  not  have  wills.   More  specifically,  40  percent  of  HRS  respondents
5:165:11417:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:report not having wills and 30 percent of HRS respondents aged 70 and over report not
5:166:11502:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:having wills.  Of HRS respondents who died, 38 percent died intestate.  Hence, the usual
5:167:11590:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:focus on bequest intentions provides an incomplete and misleading picture of end-of-life
5:168:11678:18:18:70:117:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers.
5:169:11688:18:18:88:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The paper is organized as follows.  Section 2 reviews previous work on bequests and
5:170:11771:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:describes the legal environment in which individuals make end-of-life transfers.  The data
5:171:11861:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are described in Section 3, where we also present the statistical methods we use in our
5:172:11948:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis.  Section 4 presents the benchmark results of our empirical analysis of bequest
5:173:12036:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intentions,  while  Section  5  shows  further  empirical  results,  which  include  instrumental
5:174:12133:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables estimates, and the analysis of changes in bequest intentions and of the actual
5:175:12221:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:division  of  estates.   Section  6  provides  a  simple  conceptual  framework  for  interpreting
5:176:12319:18:16:70:280:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:end-of-life transfers.  Section 7 concludes.
5:177:12363:16:15:84:524:165:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:8In a traditional nuclear family all the children in the household are joint children, but one or both
5:178:12465:15:0:70:379:150:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:parents may have children from previous partnerships living elsewhere.
6:179:12536:0:26:70:342:759:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.  Background and Related Literature
6:180:12573:26:18:70:524:733:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Almost all economic models predict unequal bequests.9For example, the altruist model
6:181:12657:18:18:70:524:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumes that parents equalize marginal utilities across children (Barro 1974; Becker 1974;
6:182:12747:18:18:70:524:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Becker  and  Tomes  1979;  Tomes  1981).   This  assumption,  together  with  some  strong
6:183:12837:18:18:70:524:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions about preferences and inter vivos transfers, implies that parents will bequeath
6:184:12928:18:18:70:524:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more  to  their  less  well-off  children.   Exchange  models  assume  that  bequests  are  made
6:185:13024:18:19:70:524:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  children  in  return  for  their  services  such  as  attention  and  care  (Bernheim,  Shleifer,
6:186:13125:19:18:70:524:624:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Summers  1985;  Cox  1987;  Cox  and  Rank  1992).   Because  children  face  different
6:187:13217:18:18:70:524:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:opportunity costs of providing these services, exchange models predict that children will
6:188:13306:18:18:70:444:588:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:provide different amounts of services and will receive unequal bequests.10
6:189:13380:18:18:88:524:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although both the altruist model and exchange models have some empirical support
6:190:13460:18:18:70:524:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Tomes  1988,  Cox  and  Rank  1992;  Laitner  and  Ohlsson  2001),  most  empirical  studies
6:191:13553:18:18:70:524:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:challenge both classes of models finding that an overwhelming majority of parents divide
6:192:13641:18:18:70:524:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their estates equally among their children (Menchik 1980, 1988; Wilhelm 1996; McGarry
6:193:13726:18:18:70:524:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1999;  Light  and  McGarry  2004;  Behrman  and  Rosenzweig  2004;  Erixson  and  Ohlsson
6:194:13815:18:18:70:524:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2015).11Significant  effort  has  then  been  devoted  to  rationalizing  equal  bequests.   For
6:195:13911:18:18:70:524:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instance, Bernheim and Severinov (2003) propose a model of intergenerational transfers
6:196:13997:18:18:70:524:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:based  on  the  assumption  that  each  child’s  perception  of  parental  affection  influences
6:197:14093:18:18:70:524:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:his or her subjective well-being.  Children cannot directly observe parental preferences,
6:198:14182:18:18:70:524:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but parents signal affection through their actions, including bequests.  Altruistic parents
6:199:14273:18:18:70:524:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then must consider the possibility that unequal bequests may lead their children to infer
6:200:14362:18:18:70:524:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  they  are  loved  either  more  or  less  than  their  siblings.   The  assumption  that  the
6:201:14461:18:18:70:524:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:division  of  inter  vivos  gifts  is  not  observed  by  all  the  children,  whereas  the  division  of
6:202:14566:18:19:70:524:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequests (or the division implied by bequest intentions) is observed,  remains untested.
6:203:14654:19:18:70:524:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Nor is it clear whether and how parents’ stated bequest intentions affect children’s actions
6:204:14746:18:18:70:524:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g.,  caregiving) regarding the parents.  Equal division is also consistent with parents’
6:205:14837:18:18:70:524:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indifference over how their estates are divided among their children.  But indifference is
6:206:14927:18:18:70:524:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both implausible and theoretically unsatisfying because it is compatible with all possible
6:207:15017:18:18:70:167:245:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:division patterns.12
6:208:15037:18:18:88:524:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Evolutionary psychology suggests a suite of hypotheses about end-of-life transfers that
6:209:15124:18:15:84:524:209:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:9Comprehensive  reviews  of  the  extensive  economics  literature  on  bequests  are  given  by  Behrman
6:210:15229:15:12:70:524:194:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(1997),  Laitner  (1997),  Laferr`ere  and  Wolff  (2006),  and  McGarry  (2008,  2013).   For  an  introduction
6:211:15341:12:12:70:524:182:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:to the legal literature, see Friedman (2009) and Grossman and Friedman (2011).  For a comprehensive
6:212:15440:12:8:70:349:170:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:treatment of the legal issues, see Dukeminier and Sitkoff (2013).
6:213:15505:8:16:80:524:162:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:10Bargaining power and bargaining ability will also play a role in the absence of special assumptions
6:214:15606:16:8:70:378:146:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(e.g., that parents can make take-it-or-leave-it offers to their children.)
6:215:15681:8:16:80:524:138:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:11Wilhelm  (1996),  which  use  federal  estate  tax  data,  does  allow  for  adopted  children  but  not  for
6:216:15792:16:12:70:524:122:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:stepchildren and assumes that parents have equal (symmetric) concern for all their children.  To the best
6:217:15897:12:8:70:494:110:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of our knowledge, all bequest models driven by altruism or exchange motives ignore stepchildren.
6:218:15993:8:16:80:524:102:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:12Pollak (1988) argues that the credibility of the parents’ threat to disinherit a child in the strategic
6:219:16098:16:12:70:524:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:bequest  model  of  Bernheim,  Shleifer,  and  Summers  (1985)  crucially  depends  on  the  assumption  that
6:220:16207:12:0:70:413:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:parents are indifferent over how their estates are divided among their children.
7:221:16288:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are still largely untested (Cox 2003, 2007).  The underlying premise is that parents behave
7:222:16379:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so as to maximize the probability of survival of their genes and that children with greater
7:223:16470:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wealth are more likely to pass on their genes.  One implication is what we call the “genetic-
7:224:16563:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:child hypothesis” — that is, parents will make end-of-life transfers to their genetic children
7:225:16657:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rather than to their social children (i.e., genetically unrelated children such as stepchildren
7:226:16752:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:who live in the same household).13We consider the implications of this hypothesis in two
7:227:16840:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cases: stepchildren and genetic children with whom the decedent has had no contact (e.g.,
7:228:16929:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children from a previous marriage who were very young when the parents divorced).  The
7:229:17015:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic child hypothesis makes clear predictions in both of these cases.  Decedents will
7:230:17103:18:18:70:219:596:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:favor their genetic children.14
7:231:17134:18:18:88:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  only  empirical  work  that  attempts  to  assess  the  relative  importance  of  the  al-
7:232:17229:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:truism, exchange, and the genetic-child hypotheses is Light and McGarry (2004).  Using
7:233:17315:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intended  bequest  data  for  a  sample  of  45-  to  80-year-old  mothers  drawn  from  the  Na-
7:234:17412:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional  Longitudinal  Surveys  of  Young  Women  and  Mature  Women,  they  find  that  the
7:235:17503:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vast  majority  of  mothers  (more  than  92  percent)  intend  to  leave  equal  bequests.   The
7:236:17600:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mothers  who  said  they  intended  to  leave  unequal  bequests  were  asked  to  explain  why.
7:237:17696:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Some  responded  with  explanations  that  were  consistent  with  altruism,  others  with  ex-
7:238:17791:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:change and,  among mothers with stepchildren,  some with explanations consistent with
7:239:17876:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the genetic-child hypothesis.  Light and McGarry find that greater within-family variation
7:240:17966:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in children’s incomes (a proxy for altruism), poor maternal health (a proxy for exchange),
7:241:18056:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the presence of stepchildren (a proxy for the genetic-child motive) are associated with
7:242:18147:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher probabilities of unequal intended bequests.  More specifically, for mothers with at
7:243:18237:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:least one genetic child and at least one stepchild, they find that the probability of unequal
7:244:18330:18:18:70:455:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intended bequests increases from 7.9 to 11.3 percent, a 43 percent increase.
7:245:18406:18:18:88:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Other studies examine the extent to which the division of end-of-life transfers com-
7:246:18490:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pensates for caregiving.  For example, using data from the first wave of the Assets and
7:247:18577:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Health Dynamics among the Oldest Old, Brown (2006) finds that children who are cur-
7:248:18660:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rently caregivers are 32 percentage points more likely than their noncaregiving siblings
7:249:18748:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be included in their parents’ life insurance policies, while expected caregivers are three
7:250:18841:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage  points  more  likely  to  be  included  in  their  parents’  wills  and  15  percentage
7:251:18940:18:16:80:524:217:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:13Unlike models based on altruism or exchange, which hinge on actions taken individually by parents
7:252:19039:16:11:70:524:201:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and children (such as the child’s need for support or the frequency of visits to and other contacts with older
7:253:19149:11:12:70:524:190:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:parents), the genetic-child hypothesis relies on one specific trait – the genetic link between decedents and
7:254:19257:12:12:70:524:178:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:potential beneficiaries.  In this respect, the genetic-child hypothesis is similar to models of intrahousehold
7:255:19367:12:12:70:524:166:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:allocation that emphasize a single (exogenous) attribute,  such as birth order (Behrman and Taubman
7:256:19466:12:12:70:524:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:1986; Chu 1991) or the child’s sex (Behrman, Pollak and Taubman 1986).  Although these other single-
7:257:19566:12:12:70:524:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:attribute models may be useful for understanding differential inter vivos transfers or bequests related to
7:258:19672:12:12:70:524:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:birth order or sex, they cannot explain unequal bequests or bequest intentions toward genetic and social
7:259:19776:12:9:70:107:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:children.
7:260:19785:9:15:80:524:109:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:14Evolutionary reasoning also speaks to the distribution of bequests among genetic children and, when
7:261:19886:15:12:70:524:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:it does, it seldom predicts equal bequests.  For example, a childless post-menopausal daughter would not
7:262:19990:12:0:70:476:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:be predicted to receive bequests.  These accounts however are outside the scope of our paper.
8:263:20084:0:18:70:441:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points more likely to be included in their parents’ life-insurance policies.
8:264:20160:18:19:88:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Unequal transfers from parents to children and from children to parents have also been
8:265:20246:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:documented in divorced families.  Analyzing the effects of parental marital disruption on
8:266:20335:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:late-life inter vivos transfers, Pezzin and Schone (1999) find that parents (especially older
8:267:20428:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:men) engage in substantially lower levels of transfers with stepchildren than with their
8:268:20516:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic children.  Marital disruption is also central in Pezzin, Pollak, and Schone (2008).
8:269:20607:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:That  study,  however,  concentrates  on  “upstream  transfers”  (i.e.,  adult  children’s  time
8:270:20703:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and cash transfers to their parents) rather than on “downstream transfers” (i.e., transfers
8:271:20794:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of time and cash from parents to their children).  They find unequal flows of services to
8:272:20883:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unpartnered disabled parents in families that experience divorce, with stepchildren pro-
8:273:20971:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:viding significantly lower transfers than genetic children.  Other than Light and McGarry
8:274:21060:18:18:70:453:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2004), however, no previous study has examined bequests to stepchildren.
8:275:21133:18:18:88:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:End-of-life transfers and bequests have also been analyzed by legal scholars and com-
8:276:21218:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mentators.  Unequal division of estates among genetic children typically generates unease
8:277:21307:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:among  trust  and  estates  lawyers  because  they  view  unequal  bequests  as  invitations  to
8:278:21403:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:litigation (Collins 2000; Blattmachr 2008; American Bar Association 2013).  Stepchildren,
8:279:21492:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however,  belong  to  a  different  category  since  the  law  treats  stepchildren  as  unrelated
8:280:21590:18:18:70:452:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strangers rather than as family members (Schanzenbach and Sitkoff 2009).
8:281:21662:18:19:88:531:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Legal scholars also write on intestacy, a subject thus far entirely neglected by economists.
8:282:21754:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intestacy statutes divide the estates of married decedents with children between the sur-
8:283:21843:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:viving spouse and the decedent’s genetic and legally adopted children.15If a stepparent
8:284:21930:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dies without a valid will,  stepchildren inherit nothing.16As a number of scholars have
8:285:22017:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pointed out, stepchildren have never fared well under intestacy statutes (Mahoney 1989;
8:286:22104:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Gary 2000; Noble 2002; Brashier 2004; Cremer 2011).  Stepchildren however may inherit
8:287:22189:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from their absent biological parent, and so it is unclear whether they are disadvantaged by
8:288:22280:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intestacy law.17This issue cannot be explored with the HRS data and requires additional
8:289:22367:18:18:70:115:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:research.
8:290:22376:18:18:88:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Some stepparents may intentionally forego writing a will precisely because they know
8:291:22460:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  intestacy  laws  will  mandate  an  equal  division  among  their  genetic  and  adopted
8:292:22554:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children and give nothing to their stepchildren.  On the other hand, parents with genetic
8:293:22643:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children  with  whom  they  have  had  no  contact  might  write  wills  to  avoid  giving  these
8:294:22740:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children an equal share of their estates.  Some parents are no doubt aware of the default
8:295:22829:18:16:80:524:181:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:15The Uniform Probate Code treats adopted children as if they were genetic children of the decedent
8:296:22928:16:8:70:182:165:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(Noble 2002; Cahn 2005).
8:297:22952:8:16:80:524:157:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:16California provides a narrow exception to this generalization:  a stepchild may inherit if it can be
8:298:23054:16:11:70:524:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:shown that the stepparent would have adopted the stepchild but was prevented from doing so by a legal
8:299:23155:11:12:70:524:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:barrier.  This exception is available only to a stepchild who satisfies the legal definition of a stepchild
8:300:23262:12:12:70:524:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(i.e., a child of the decedent’s spouse, not of the decedent’s cohabiting partner).  See Hanson (1995) and
8:301:23368:12:9:70:201:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Noble (2002) for more details.
8:302:23398:9:15:80:524:97:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:17At common law, in fact, the relationship of stepparent and stepchild generally confers no rights and
8:303:23500:15:0:70:222:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:imposes no duties (Wypyski 1984).
9:304:23534:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:division  imposed  by  intestacy  law  while  others  are  not.   Unfortunately,  HRS  provides
9:305:23629:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no information about respondents’ knowledge of or beliefs about intestacy law.  We can,
9:306:23716:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  the  first  time,  examine  whether  parents  are  less  likely  to  write  a  will  if  they  have
9:307:23820:18:39:70:492:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchildren or if they have genetic children with whom they have had no contact.
9:308:23901:39:26:70:124:665:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.  Data
9:309:23909:26:25:70:261:639:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A. Samples:  Core and Exit Files
9:310:23941:25:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our analysis uses data collected between 1995 and 2010 by the Health and Retirement
9:311:24024:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Study (HRS), which contains detailed information about bequest intentions and the actual
9:312:24112:18:18:70:523:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of estates.18The HRS is a longitudinal survey of a nationally representative
9:313:24201:18:19:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample of more than 26,000 Americans over the age of 50 who are interviewed every two
9:314:24286:19:18:70:524:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:years.19If a respondent has a spouse or partner, the spouse or partner is invited to become
9:315:24377:18:18:70:524:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an  HRS  respondent.   In  each  survey  year,  the  “core  files”  provide  data  from  standard
9:316:24474:18:18:70:524:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:questionnaires administered to all respondents. The “exit files” provide information about
9:317:24564:18:18:70:524:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the actual distribution of the estates of HRS respondents who died since the previous wave;
9:318:24655:18:18:70:524:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this information is collected from a proxy respondent, such as the surviving spouse, an
9:319:24742:18:18:70:297:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adult child, or another close family member.
9:320:24786:18:18:88:524:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:From the core files we select respondents with at least one child and with nonmiss-
9:321:24869:18:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing information on intended bequests and other basic variables.  This leaves us with an
9:322:24956:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unbalanced panel of 23,984 individuals, for a total of 117,189 person-wave observations.
9:323:25044:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:When first observed in the study,  11,221 individuals (47 percent of the sample) report
9:324:25131:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:having no will, while 12,763 report having a will.  As the survey progresses, the percent-
9:325:25221:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age of individuals without a will decreases to 42 percent.  Of the 21,140 parents in our
9:326:25309:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample with more than one child, 11,170 (53 percent) report their plans to distribute their
9:327:25400:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estates among their children.  More than one fifth of the whole sample (5,082 parents)
9:328:25486:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:report having both genetic children and stepchildren.20Of these individuals, 2,342 report
9:329:25575:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:having a will (about 18 percent of the sample of parents with wills or over 46 percent of
9:330:25664:18:19:70:228:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the parents with stepchildren).
9:331:25695:19:18:88:524:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The HRS also collects information on the frequency of contacts between parents and
9:332:25777:18:18:70:524:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children.  We use this information for the 12,739 individuals who have genetic children
9:333:25864:18:18:70:524:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only and report the frequency of contacts with their children and their bequest intentions.
9:334:25955:18:18:70:524:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Almost 14 percent of them (1,764 parents) report having had no contact with at least one
9:335:26043:18:18:70:524:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of their genetic children for at least one year during the survey period.  On average 6.6
9:336:26132:18:15:80:524:144:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:18As noted in the Introduction, HRS asks respondents about their bequest intentions only if they report
9:337:26235:15:12:70:524:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:having wills or trusts.  We do not distinguish between wills and trusts, because trusts are not common in
9:338:26340:12:12:70:524:117:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the HRS sample:  only 1.1 percent of the respondents report having a trust but not a will and 1.4 percent
9:339:26445:12:8:70:235:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:report having both a will and a trust.
9:340:26483:8:12:80:423:97:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:19See<http://hrsonline.isr.umich.edu/>for more information about the data.
9:341:26557:12:0:80:428:85:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:20The HRS does not distinguish between genetic children and adopted children.
10:342:26635:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent of parents report having no contact in the previous year with at least one of their
10:343:26726:18:19:70:523:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children.21Among no-contact parents, the proportion without a will exceeds 57 percent.
10:344:26812:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is substantially greater than that observed among parents who have more frequent
10:345:26897:18:18:70:332:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact with all their genetic children (43 percent).
10:346:26950:18:18:88:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The exit files provide information on the actual disposition of estates and other basic
10:347:27037:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables  for  7,416  individuals  (almost  85  percent)  of  the  8,800  HRS  respondents  who
10:348:27133:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:died over the sample period.  There are 2,781 parents (38 percent) who died intestate, a
10:349:27221:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:slightly smaller proportion than the 42 percent of HRS respondents in the core files who
10:350:27309:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:report having no wills.  Of the remaining 4,635 who died with a will, 3,897 had more than
10:351:27398:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one child and 630 (18 percent of the sample of decedents with wills and with more than
10:352:27484:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one child) had both stepchildren and genetic children, representing more than 90 percent
10:353:27572:18:35:70:237:560:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of decedents with stepchildren.22
10:354:27605:35:26:70:146:525:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B. Outcomes
10:355:27616:26:18:70:524:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Table 1 shows the means of our main dependent variables broken down by the presence
10:356:27699:18:18:70:524:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of stepchildren in both the core and the exit files and by parents’ marital status.  About
10:357:27789:18:18:70:524:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:42  percent  of  the  sample  in  the  core  files  does  not  have  a  will  (column  (a)).   The  raw
10:358:27892:18:18:70:524:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference  of  6.9  percentage  points  between  those  with  stepchildren  (column  (b))  and
10:359:27987:18:18:70:524:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those  with  genetic  children  only  (column  (c))  is  statistically  significant.   Almost  two-
10:360:28086:18:18:70:524:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thirds of divorced parents do not have a will.  Again, parents with stepchildren are less
10:361:28175:18:18:70:524:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to have a will than parents with genetic children only.  The same picture emerges
10:362:28263:18:18:70:524:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from  the  exit  files,  even  though  the  fraction  of  all  parents  without  a  will  is  almost  38
10:363:28367:18:18:70:524:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent, somewhat less than in the core files.  We shall return to this issue in the next
10:364:28456:18:18:70:108:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:section.
10:365:28464:18:18:88:524:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Conditional on having a will, about three-quarters of the parents from the core files
10:366:28549:18:18:70:524:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:report they include all children in their wills, while only 59 percent of the estates whose
10:367:28640:18:18:70:524:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions are reported in the exit files were divided in a way that included all chil-
10:368:28730:18:18:70:524:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren.23Intended inclusion of all children is substantially less likely among parents with
10:369:28819:18:18:70:524:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchildren regardless of their marital status, but this does not emerge in the exit files,
10:370:28911:18:16:80:524:229:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:21Among parents with both stepchildren and genetic children, the proportion of parents with no contact
10:371:29013:16:8:70:318:213:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:with at least one of their children is higher, around 28%.
10:372:29071:8:16:80:524:205:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:22The exit files necessarily yield a sample that is smaller than that obtained from the core files.  More-
10:373:29177:16:12:70:524:189:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:over, at present, the exit files disproportionally represent individuals with lower socioeconomic status and
10:374:29285:12:8:70:255:177:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:higher mortality risks (Cutler et al.  2011).
10:375:29330:8:16:80:524:169:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:23As  already  mentioned,  most  of  the  information  available  in  the  HRS  is  on  bequest  intentions  of
10:376:29441:16:12:70:524:153:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:parents who report that they have a will.  The exception is in relation to the probability that respondents
10:377:29548:12:12:70:524:141:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:bequeath a specific amount of money (expressed in given categories), which is asked to each household
10:378:29649:12:11:70:524:129:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:independently of whether respondents have a will or not.  At the end of subsection 4.B we discuss the
10:379:29750:11:12:70:524:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:results  found  using  that  information.   We  should  stress  that  this  information  is  not  about  the  exact
10:380:29865:12:12:70:524:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:monetary  value  of  resources  that  parents  intend  to  transfer  to  their  children.   Rather,  it  is  about  the
10:381:29984:12:12:70:524:94:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f6:F:probabilitythat a parent leaves a bequest worth a given amount of money.  We therefore cannot determine
10:382:30087:12:0:70:369:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:how much each child will inherit in case his/her parents write a will.
11:383:30158:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where none of the differences are statistically significant at conventional levels (column
11:384:30248:18:19:70:140:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(d), panel B).
11:385:30262:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the core files, almost one-third of all parents with a will report that they plan to
11:386:30349:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribute their estate unequally among their children (column (a),  panel  C).  Intended
11:387:30438:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unequal divisions are much more likely among parents with stepchildren (61 percent for all
11:388:30528:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents and a staggering 75 percent for divorced parents, column (b)) than among parents
11:389:30616:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with genetic children only (27 and 29 percent respectively, column (c)).  In the exit files,
11:390:30708:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however,  the  proportion  of  estates  that  are  divided  unequally  is  substantially  greater
11:391:30805:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(53 percent).  The difference between parents with stepchildren and parents with genetic
11:392:30893:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children  only  is  smaller  than  that  observed  in  the  core  files,  but  is  always  statistically
11:393:30997:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant.  This may reflect a change in parents’ behavior between the time they reported
11:394:31088:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their intentions in the core files and the actual distribution of their estates reported in the
11:395:31183:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exit files.  It may also be driven by selection (parents in the exit files are older) or reflect
11:396:31279:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the difference in mortality rates by socioeconomic status (parents in the exit files are less
11:397:31372:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:educated and less healthy, and these might be the type of parents who are more likely to
11:398:31460:18:18:70:313:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribute unequally their end-of-life resources).
11:399:31510:18:18:88:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Appendix Table A1 mirrors Table 1 focusing on no-contact parents.  As in the case of
11:400:31594:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents with stepchildren, parents who have had no contact with their genetic children
11:401:31680:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the past year are much more likely not to have a will.  About 59 percent of no-contact
11:402:31769:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents have no will, as opposed to 44 percent of parents who have regular contact with
11:403:31856:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all their genetic children (panel A). Among divorced no-contact parents the proportion
11:404:31942:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  those  without  a  will  is  70  percent.   Looking  only  at  parents  with  a  will,  almost  84
11:405:32044:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent of those with regular contacts with all their genetic children report the intention
11:406:32135:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to include all of them in the will.  This proportion is 27 percentage points greater than
11:407:32224:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that observed among no-contact parents,  and the difference is highly significant (panel
11:408:32312:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:B). Finally, parents in regular contact with their children also report they are more likely
11:409:32404:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than no-contact parents to divide their estates equally (77 and 47 percent, respectively).
11:410:32494:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The difference between these two groups of parents is even greater when we consider those
11:411:32583:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:who divorced or widowed (panel C). These patterns are consistent with the predictions
11:412:32668:18:35:70:217:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implied by exchange models.
11:413:32695:35:26:70:364:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:C. Explanatory Variables and Statistical Methods
11:414:32743:26:18:70:524:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Table 2 reports summary statistics for the explanatory variables we use to model the prob-
11:415:32833:18:18:70:524:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:abilities of reporting having a will and reporting the intention to leave unequal bequests.
11:416:32924:18:18:70:524:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We show figures for the sample of parents who report having wills (column (b)) and for
11:417:33010:18:18:70:524:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the broader sample of 23,984 individuals that also includes parents who report not having
11:418:33099:18:18:70:524:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wills (column (a)).  The table also presents summary statistics for the subsample of all
11:419:33187:18:0:70:524:84:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents who have both genetic children and stepchildren (column (c)) and the subsample
12:420:33275:0:18:70:450:759:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of 2,342 parents with stepchildren who report having wills (column (d)).24
12:421:33349:18:19:88:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our covariates include standard demographic controls for parents’ age, sex, race, mar-
12:422:33435:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ital status, and number of marriages.  These variables capture basic heterogeneity within
12:423:33524:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and across households. We also include measures of annual family income and total wealth
12:424:33612:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(both expressed in 1995 prices), parents’ education and employment status.  We use these
12:425:33700:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables as controls for heterogeneity in parental resources.  HRS respondents are also
12:426:33788:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asked whether they gave money to at least one child or to all children equally; inter vivos
12:427:33879:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers are known to depend more directly than bequests on children’s current incomes
12:428:33966:18:18:70:360:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and thus tend to be divided less evenly (McGarry 1999).
12:429:34021:18:18:88:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One of our key explanatory variables is an indicator variable for the presence of at
12:430:34105:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:least one genetic child and at least one stepchild.  The genetic-child hypothesis predicts
12:431:34195:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that parents will treat genetic children and stepchildren differently in allocating resources.
12:432:34289:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Because parents’ ability or willingness to make transfers may depend on the total number
12:433:34377:18:18:70:421:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of children and stepchildren, we include these characteristics as well.
12:434:34448:18:18:88:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another key variable is parents’ lack of contact with their genetic children.  Parents
12:435:34534:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:who  report  having  had  no  contact  with  at  least  one  of  their  genetic  children  over  the
12:436:34634:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previous year are defined to be no-contact parents.  In subsection 5.D we will also consider
12:437:34726:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents with infrequent contact.  This latter group comprises parents who report having
12:438:34813:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:had at least one contact with their children over the last year, but not at least one contact
12:439:34906:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a month, while parents with frequent contacts are those who have contact at least once a
12:440:34994:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:month.  Exchange models predict that children with more regular contacts will be more
12:441:35079:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to receive bequests if these children are also more likely to provide care and support
12:442:35172:18:18:70:482:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to their needy older parents (Bernheim, Shleifer, and Summers 1985; Cox 1987).
12:443:35250:18:18:88:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We use parental health status (“poor or fair” as opposed to “good or excellent”) as
12:444:35333:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a proxy for a parent’s need for children’s services and hence, willingness to pay for them
12:445:35423:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e., the exchange motive).  Using the parents’ reports of the children’s income and wealth
12:446:35515:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would substantially reduce the number of observations, so instead of doing so we predict
12:447:35603:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each child’s income using observed characteristics.  Following Light and McGarry (2004),
12:448:35691:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we  predict  incomes  using  estimated  parameters  from  income  models  that  we  fit  to  the
12:449:35787:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data  from  the  Current  Population  Survey  (CPS)  between  1994  and  2006.   Our  sample
12:450:35879:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consists of all CPS respondents in the same age group as the parents/children in our HRS
12:451:35967:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample.  We estimate separate models for men and women using as regressors a constant,
12:452:36053:18:18:70:524:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a quartic in age, five dummy variables indicating the highest educational attainment, and
12:453:36142:18:18:70:524:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indicator variables for race, marital status, number of children, and home ownership.  We
12:454:36231:18:18:70:524:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then use this predicted income variable to construct a measure of income differences, the
12:455:36320:18:18:70:524:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient of variation (obtained by dividing the standard deviation of estimated income
12:456:36409:18:19:70:335:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by its mean) among the children of each individual.
12:457:36460:19:16:80:524:90:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:24For the sake of brevity, summary statistics of the independent variables for the sample of contact/no-
12:458:36564:16:0:70:405:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:contact parents are not reported.  They are available on the online appendix.
13:459:36643:0:18:88:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For each of our covariates, we observe differences between parents with a will, parents
13:460:36730:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with stepchildren, and parents with stepchildren and a will (columns (b)–(d)).  Perhaps
13:461:36817:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unsurprisingly, the most striking differences are between parents in the core files (column
13:462:36908:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(a)) and those in the exit files (column (e)).  Compared with the parents in the core files,
13:463:37000:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents in the exit files are less educated and more likely to report being in poor or fair
13:464:37091:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:health in the last wave in which they participated.  Parents in the exit files are older (and
13:465:37184:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus more likely to be retired), and more likely to have been widowed (and hence to have
13:466:37272:18:30:70:199:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower household income).
13:467:37296:30:18:70:524:602:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:Methods— LetYitdenote one of the outcome variables described in subsection 3.B above,
13:468:37381:18:18:70:524:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:i.e.,  whether  individualidoes  not  have  a  will  at  timet(=1,  0  otherwise),  whetheri,
13:469:37474:18:18:70:524:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional on having a will, mentions all children in the will at timet(=1, 0 otherwise),
13:470:37564:18:18:70:524:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  whetheriincludes  all  children  equally  in  the  will  (=1,  0  otherwise).   LetXitbe
13:471:37657:18:18:70:523:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a matrix containing all the explanatory variables described above, andCitan indicator
13:472:37742:18:18:70:524:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variable that is equal to 1 if individualilives in a complex family (i.e., stepfamily or no-
13:473:37834:18:18:70:524:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact family) at timet, and zero otherwise.  In the next section we report and discuss
13:474:37922:18:18:70:524:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:random effects (RE) probit estimates obtained from a specification of the following sort
13:475:38010:18:33:70:246:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Arellano 2003; Wooldridge 2010):
13:476:38043:33:33:100:524:425:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:A:Yit=α+βCit+X′itγ+εit,(1)
13:477:38067:33:18:70:524:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereεit=νi+ξitis  the  residual,  in  whichνiis  the  unobserved  individual-specific
13:478:38153:18:18:70:321:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:component andξitis an idiosyncratic error term.
13:479:38200:18:18:88:524:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since the RE model assumes thatνiandCit(as well asνiandXit) are uncorrelated,
13:480:38277:18:18:70:524:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in subsection 5.A we shall present results based on fixed effects (FE) models, which do
13:481:38364:18:18:70:524:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not  impose  this  no-correlation  assumption.   In  the  same  subsection,  we  also  deal  with
13:482:38461:18:18:70:524:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the potential endogeneity of family complexity by using an instrumental variables (IV)
13:483:38547:18:18:70:523:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:method based on a new instrument forCit.  We defer the description of this approach to
13:484:38633:18:40:70:186:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that part of the paper.
13:485:38656:40:25:70:244:226:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.  Benchmark Estimates
13:486:38679:25:18:70:524:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We present our benchmark estimates, emphasizing the roles of stepparents and parents
13:487:38763:18:18:70:524:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:without  contact  with  at  least  one  of  their  genetic  children.   We  first  describe  who  has
13:488:38864:18:18:70:524:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  will  and  who  does  not  (subsection  A).  Then  we  analyze  whether  parents  include  all
13:489:38961:18:19:70:524:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children in the will and,  if they do,  whether they intend to leave equal bequests to all
13:490:39051:19:18:70:524:128:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children  (subsection  B).25We  next  investigate  how  health,  wealth,  and  previous  inter
13:491:39145:18:18:70:524:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vivos transfers affect the probability that HRS respondents intend to treat their children
13:492:39235:18:18:70:201:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unequally (subsection C).
13:493:39260:18:0:80:392:74:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:25It is worth keeping in mind that stepchildren are counted as children.
14:494:39334:0:26:70:303:759:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A. Who Has a Will and Who Does Not
14:495:39368:26:18:70:524:733:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As  we  saw  in  Table  1,  the  fraction  of  HRS  respondents  who  have  children  but  do  not
14:496:39466:18:18:70:524:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have wills is substantial:  42 percent of those in the core files report not having a will.
14:497:39557:18:18:70:524:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A  complication  with  bequest  intention  data  is  right  censoring:  some  parents  who  will
14:498:39653:18:18:70:524:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eventually write wills have not done so at the time they respond to the survey.  Older and
14:499:39743:18:18:70:524:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less healthy parents, however, might be more likely than other respondents to write wills.
14:500:39833:18:19:70:524:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:So might unpartnered widows or widowers, who are the last ones to have the responsibility
14:501:39922:19:18:70:524:624:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of passing on the family estate to future generations.  To account for these possibilities, we
14:502:40016:18:18:70:524:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:control for parental age and health status, and estimate separately the response of widows,
14:503:40107:18:18:70:524:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:widowers and divorced parents.  To assess the extent of the right censoring problem more
14:504:40195:18:18:70:281:570:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:directly, we use data from the exit files.26
14:505:40239:18:18:88:524:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 3 presents marginal effects from random effects probit estimates ofβin equation
14:506:40324:18:18:70:524:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1), that is, the impact of the presence of stepchildren on the probability that parents re-
14:507:40416:18:18:70:524:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portnothaving a will.  The table, based on data from the core files, shows the results from
14:508:40507:18:18:70:524:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:five specifications.  In specification (a) we include our basic set of controls (demographics,
14:509:40601:18:18:70:524:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:education, and employment status) as well as health status indicators.  Specification (b)
14:510:40690:18:18:70:524:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adds  measures  of  money  transfers  to  children,  while  specification  (c)  drops  these  mea-
14:511:40788:18:18:70:524:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sures of money transfers but includes controls for parents’ expected income and wealth.
14:512:40875:18:18:70:524:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Specification (d) includes all previous measures,  while specification (e) also includes as
14:513:40966:18:18:70:524:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an additional regressor the coefficient of variation between children’s income.  Besides the
14:514:41058:18:18:70:524:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results for all parents, the table also shows results separately for fathers and for mothers,
14:515:41151:18:18:70:524:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and reports the pooled and separate effects for the subsamples of widowed and divorced
14:516:41237:18:18:70:111:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents.
14:517:41245:18:19:88:524:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although the descriptive statistics show that individuals with both genetic children
14:518:41329:19:18:70:524:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and stepchildren are less likely to report having wills than those with genetic children only,
14:519:41423:18:18:70:524:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the estimates in Table 3 imply that our basic control variables largely account for this
14:520:41511:18:18:70:524:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference (column (a)), except for widows and for divorced fathers.  Widows are indeed 7
14:521:41600:18:18:70:524:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points more likely to have a will.  This is confirmed when we control for inter
14:522:41690:18:18:70:524:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vivos transfers and parental income and wealth (columns (b)–(d)), but the relationship
14:523:41776:18:18:70:524:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:becomes weaker and loses statistical significance when we further control for the coefficient
14:524:41869:18:18:70:389:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of variation between children’s predicted income (column (e)).
14:525:41931:18:18:88:524:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For  divorced  fathers  with  stepchildren  we  find  that  the  probability  of  not  having  a
14:526:42027:18:18:70:524:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will is nearly 8 percentage points greater than the corresponding probability for divorced
14:527:42117:18:18:70:524:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fathers with genetic children only (column (a)).  Controlling for inter vivos transfers and
14:528:42208:18:18:70:524:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parental income and wealth leads to even greater estimates, ranging from 8 to 12 percent-
14:529:42297:18:16:80:524:119:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:26As mentioned in Section 3, 38 percent of parents in the exit files died intestate.  This slightly lower
14:530:42402:16:11:70:524:103:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:proportion  than  that  recorded  in  the  core  files  may  reflect  an  actual  change  in  parents’  behavior  or
14:531:42518:11:12:70:524:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:selection driven by differential attrition based on age, health, and socioeconomic status.  We leave this
14:532:42623:12:0:70:226:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:interesting issue for future research.
15:533:42663:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age points (columns (b) to (d)).  When we control for within-family income differences,
15:534:42750:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the probability of not having a will goes up to almost 20 percentage points.  In the next
15:535:42839:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subsection we examine whether the differential propensities to have a will reflect parental
15:536:42930:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:preferences  to  favor  own  genetic  children  or  preferences  to  equalize  the  distribution  of
15:537:43030:18:18:70:323:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estates across all children, including stepchildren.
15:538:43082:18:18:88:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 4 broadly confirms the results found for stepparents in the case of no-contact
15:539:43166:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents.  There are however two differences.  One is among fathers who are 10–12 per-
15:540:43251:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:centage points more likely not to have a will if they have no contact with their genetic
15:541:43339:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children, although this relationship disappears when we control for expected wealth and
15:542:43426:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:within-family income differences.  The other difference is among widowers who, regard-
15:543:43512:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less of the specification, are between 14 and 20 percentage points more likely to have no
15:544:43601:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will if they have no contact with their genetic children.  Lack of contact therefore may
15:545:43689:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:induce fathers in general, and widowers in particular, to eschew the allocations implied
15:546:43777:18:18:70:179:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by intestacy statutes.
15:547:43799:18:18:88:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We do not know, however, why so many individuals do not write wills.  Legal scholars
15:548:43883:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggest that procrastination is one of the most plausible explanations for intestacy (Weis-
15:549:43974:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bord 2012).  But procrastination does not manifest an intent to die intestate.  Likewise,
15:550:44063:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the high rate of intestacy is not the result of agreement with, or reliance on, the default
15:551:44154:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rules of heirship.  Although agreement with the default rules could reduce the need for a
15:552:44243:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will (Hirsch 2004), there is some (dated) anecdotal evidence that suggests that individu-
15:553:44332:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:als lacking a will do not intentionally rely on the default rules (Fellows, Simon, and Rau
15:554:44422:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1978; Contemporary Studies Project 1978).  Economists have also been moving away from
15:555:44507:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the notion that individuals who do not “opt out” could be assumed to prefer the default
15:556:44594:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Thaler and Sunstein 2008).  For example, in the context of retirement savings, Beshears
15:557:44682:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al.  (2009) provide strong empirical evidence that defaults do matter.  In the context
15:558:44771:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of intestacy, we have no empirical research to draw on.  Nonetheless, the earlier evidence
15:559:44861:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used by legal experts and the empirical evidence found in other contexts argue against
15:560:44947:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assuming that individuals without wills prefer, and would have chosen, the distribution
15:561:45034:18:35:70:211:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mandated by intestacy law.
15:562:45060:35:26:70:250:218:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B. Unequal Intended Bequests
15:563:45088:26:18:70:524:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Conditional on parents having a will and having more than one child, we now investigate
15:564:45175:18:18:70:524:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two questions:  whether parentsincludeall children in their wills and whether they treat
15:565:45263:18:18:70:239:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all childrenequallyin their wills.
15:566:45297:18:18:88:524:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 5 presents random effects probit estimates of the stepchild variable on the proba-
15:567:45385:18:18:70:524:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bility that individuals include all children in their wills.  The five specifications in columns
15:568:45481:18:18:70:524:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(a)–(e) and the rest of the organization of the table are the same as in Table 3.  Table
15:569:45569:18:0:70:524:84:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:5 reveals that for parents with stepchildren the likelihood of including all children in the
16:570:45663:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will is 28–39 percentage points lower than for parents without stepchildren.  This impact
16:571:45752:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is stronger in absolute value for mothers than for fathers, although controlling for income
16:572:45843:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dispersion between siblings reverses this result (column (e)).  In specification (d), moth-
16:573:45934:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ers with stepchildren are almost 38 percentage points less likely to report including all
16:574:46023:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children in their wills while fathers with stepchildren are about 27 percentage points less
16:575:46114:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to do so.  These negative effects are strongest for divorced parents with stepchil-
16:576:46204:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren,  with estimated impacts ranging between 59 and 63 percentage points lower than
16:577:46288:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  divorced  parents  without  stepchildren.   We  also  find  strong  negative  effects  among
16:578:46385:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:widows and widowers.  This might happen because widows and widowers write new wills
16:579:46468:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:after the death of the spouse.  We shall return to this possibility in subsection 5.B, where
16:580:46560:18:18:70:283:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we analyze changes in bequest intentions.
16:581:46601:18:18:88:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  repeated  the  same  analysis  focusing  on  the  behavior  of  parents  who  have  only
16:582:46693:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic  children  but  who  have  no  contact  with  at  least  one  of  them.   The  results  are
16:583:46792:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:presented in Appendix Table A2.  These are qualitatively very similar to those reported
16:584:46879:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Table 5.  Parents who have no contact with at least one of their genetic children are
16:585:46967:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:20–24  percentage  points  less  likely  to  include  all  children  in  the  will.   In  this  case,  it
16:586:47072:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is fathers (and not mothers) who generally have a higher propensity not to mention all
16:587:47158:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children in their wills.  Divorced parents (especially divorced fathers) show an even greater
16:588:47251:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood of not including all of their children in the will, although this likelihood is the
16:589:47345:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:same as that found for all parents once we control for within-family differences (column
16:590:47433:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e)).  No-contact parents therefore have a substantially greater propensity to treat their
16:591:47523:18:18:70:206:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic children unequally.
16:592:47550:18:18:88:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Conditional on having a will, we repeated the same analysis for the likelihood of having
16:593:47638:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a will in which all children are treated equally.  Table 6 reports the RE probit estimates for
16:594:47732:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents with stepchildren, while Appendix Table A3 reports the estimates for no-contact
16:595:47819:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents.  Table 6 indicates that the presence of stepchildren is always associated with a
16:596:47908:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considerably lower probability of equal intended bequests and these differences are always
16:597:47998:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:statistically significant at the 1 percent level.  For example, having both genetic children
16:598:48090:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and stepchildren as opposed to having genetic children only reduces the probability of a
16:599:48178:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will in which all children are treated equally by 31 percentage points (first row, column
16:600:48267:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(d)).  This negative effect is greater for mothers than for fathers (36 versus 25 percentage
16:601:48359:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points, respectively), and the difference is statistically significant at conventional levels.
16:602:48453:18:18:70:524:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:But, as in Table 5, this gender difference is not robust to the inclusion of the coefficient
16:603:48545:18:18:70:357:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of variation of children’s predicted income (column (e)).
16:604:48602:18:18:88:524:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Unpartnered parents (either divorced or widowed) are generally less likely to plan equal
16:605:48690:18:18:70:524:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequests  if they have genetic  children  and stepchildren.  For  example,  divorced fathers
16:606:48782:18:19:70:524:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are 52 percentage points less likely to treat all children equally than divorced fathers with
16:607:48875:19:18:70:524:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic  children  only  (column  (d)).   Similar  responses  are  found  for  divorced  mothers
16:608:48971:18:0:70:524:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as  well  as  for  widows  and  widowers,  and  the  gender  differences  are  never  statistically
17:609:49072:0:18:70:125:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant.
17:610:49084:18:19:88:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Without exceptions, the estimates in Appendix Table A3 reveal that parents who have
17:611:49167:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no contact with their genetic children are also less likely to plan an equal division of their
