17:612:49261:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estates.   Parental  absence  is  on  average  associated  with  a  reduction  in  the  probability
17:613:49360:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  equal  bequest  intentions  of  28–32  percentage  points.   Slightly  larger  reductions  are
17:614:49458:18:18:70:463:668:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:observed among all fathers and among those who are divorced or widowed.27
17:615:49531:18:18:88:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In sum,  the estimates in Tables 5 and 6 and those in Appendix Tables A2 and A3
17:616:49610:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tell  a  consistent  story.   Parents  in  complex  families  are  less  likely  to  mention  all  their
17:617:49714:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children in the will.  Among such parents,  those who do mention all children are more
17:618:49800:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely  to  plan  an  unequal  division  of  end-of-life  transfers.   This  evidence  suggests  that
17:619:49901:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchildren and genetic children with no contact with their parents appear to face similar
17:620:49992:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:chances of inheriting from their stepparents and parents.  This result sits at odds with
17:621:50080:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the genetic-child hypothesis, according to which parents favor their own genetic offspring
17:622:50170:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over stepchildren, and seems instead to be driven mainly by other motives.  In the next
17:623:50257:18:35:70:310:506:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:subsection we explore this possibility further.28
17:624:50306:35:26:70:337:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:C. Health, Wealth, and Inter Vivos Transfers
17:625:50350:26:18:70:524:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our analysis we included variables that are meant to proxy altruism and exchange as
17:626:50436:18:18:70:524:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequest motives.  We also controlled for gifts to children, since parents might adjust their
17:627:50528:18:18:70:524:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequest intentions if they made substantial inter vivos transfers.  The adjustment could
17:628:50616:18:18:70:524:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:go in either direction.  Parents might give less to children who already received inter vivos
17:629:50709:18:18:70:524:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers to equalize lifetime transfers, or they might give more because previous transfers
17:630:50801:18:18:70:524:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indicate greater need or closer ties.  We now briefly discuss these results that can be found
17:631:50894:18:18:70:188:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the online appendix.
17:632:50917:18:18:88:524:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In families with stepparents and in families with no-contact parents, wealth and income
17:633:51004:18:16:80:524:301:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:27The results in Tables 6 and A3 were found for parents with two or more childrenanda will.  An
17:634:51099:16:12:70:524:285:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:alternative sample selection is to include only parents with two or more children and a will that mentions
17:635:51205:12:12:70:524:273:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f6:F:allof the children.  This selection clearly leads to smaller samples.  But even when this more restrictive
17:636:51311:12:11:70:524:261:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:definition is used, we find effect estimates that are in line with (albeit of smaller magnitude than) those
17:637:51418:11:9:70:373:250:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:shown in Tables 6 and A3.  They are reported in Appendix Table A4.
17:638:51484:9:15:80:524:241:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:28It  should  be  emphasized  that  we  performed  several  robustness  checks.   The  estimates  from  these
17:639:51593:15:12:70:524:226:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:exercises by and large confirm the picture of bequest intentions that has emerged so far.  In one of the
17:640:51697:12:12:70:524:214:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:exercises, we disaggregated the overall effect of the stepchild indicator variable by the number of genetic
17:641:51804:12:12:70:524:202:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:children and stepchildren and distinguished among parents with one child in each category, those with two
17:642:51909:12:12:70:524:190:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:genetic children and one stepchild, those with one genetic child and two stepchildren, and those with two
17:643:52014:12:12:70:524:178:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:or more children in each category.  Virtually all our earlier results are robust to this change.  In another
17:644:52122:12:12:70:524:166:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:check, we took advantage of the fact that, regardless of whether individuals have a will, the HRS asks one
17:645:52228:12:12:70:524:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:respondent per household to report the probability of leaving a bequest worth at least $10,000, $100,000,
17:646:52333:12:12:70:524:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and $500,000, excluding any inheritance to be left to the surviving partner if he/she is still alive.  We
17:647:52438:12:12:70:524:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:banded all answers into six groups, i.e., we distinguished individuals who report a zero probability from
17:648:52543:12:12:70:524:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:those with a positive probability, and these in turn were banded into five quintiles.  Using random-effects
17:649:52650:12:12:70:524:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:ordered probit regressions, we then re-analyzed the models of having a will, inclusion of all children in
17:650:52755:12:12:70:524:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the will, and equal intended bequests.  Again, the results from this analysis are qualitatively very similar
17:651:52863:12:0:70:490:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:to those discussed above.  These and the previous estimates are reported in the online appendix.
18:652:52961:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have opposite effects on the probability of having a will.  Wealthier parents are less likely
18:653:53054:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to report not having a will.  But higher income parents are more likely to do so, perhaps
18:654:53143:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because such parents are likely to be younger and still in the labor force.  In both types
18:655:53233:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of families, having made inter vivos transfers is associated with a 5–9 percentage point
18:656:53321:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduction in the probability of not having a will.  Being in fair or poor health is associated
18:657:53415:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with  a  5–10  percentage  point  increase  for  stepparents,  while  the  estimated  increase  is
18:658:53513:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:9–13 percentage points for no-contact parents.  Less healthy parents, who might be more
18:659:53600:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in need of care from their children, may have an incentive to have a will.  Finally, larger
18:660:53691:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differences in children’s incomes are associated with a higher probability of not having a
18:661:53781:18:18:70:392:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will, although this relationship is never statistically significant.
18:662:53849:18:18:88:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Wealthier stepparents and wealthier no-contact parents are more likely to report in-
18:663:53933:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cluding all children in their wills as well as dividing their estates equally.  Moreover, for
18:664:54026:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents with stepchildren, greater parental income, which might be more common among
18:665:54110:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:younger (still working) parents, is associated with a reduction in both probabilities.  For
18:666:54201:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such parents, we also estimate that parents who have already made inter vivos transfers
18:667:54288:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have a 7 percentage point higher probability of including all children in their wills and 11
18:668:54380:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage point higher probability of intending equal bequests.  For no-contact parents,
18:669:54469:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the relationship with income is weaker and the effect of inter vivos transfers is smaller.
18:670:54559:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For instance, having already made inter vivos transfers increases the probability of includ-
18:671:54651:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing all children in the will by 4–5 percentage points and the probability of equal bequest
18:672:54741:18:18:70:255:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intentions by 5–7 percentage points.
18:673:54777:18:18:88:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For both types of families, greater income dispersion between siblings is associated with
18:674:54866:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a lower probability that wills include all children and a greater probability that parents
18:675:54956:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intend to divide their estates unequally.  Although these correlations are not statistically
18:676:55048:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant, if we assume that parents intend to give more to low-income children, then
18:677:55135:18:18:70:294:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they are consistent with altruistic behavior.
18:678:55180:18:18:88:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Parents in poor health are 2 to 4 percentage points less likely to include all children
18:679:55267:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the will and, conditional on mentioning all children, around 4 percentage points less
18:680:55355:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to include all of them equally.  If poor health reflects parents’ long-term need for
18:681:55446:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:child assistance, these results suggest that parents may use their intended future transfers,
18:682:55539:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which they could make known to their children, to elicit a long-term flow of services.  This
18:683:55631:18:39:70:493:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is consistent with the exchange motive documented by Light and McGarry (2004).
18:684:55709:39:26:70:274:160:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.  Further Empirical Results
18:685:55738:26:18:70:524:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In this section we discuss further results in four subsections.  Specifically, in subsection
18:686:55830:18:18:70:524:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A we compare our benchmark RE estimates with the estimates found with FE models
18:687:55909:18:18:70:524:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  those  found  with  an  instrumental  variables  approach.   In  subsection  B  we  exploit
18:688:56005:18:0:70:524:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  longitudinal  aspect  of  the  HRS  examining  changes  in  bequest  intentions,  while  in
19:689:56103:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subsection C we turn from bequest intentions to the actual division of estates using the
19:690:56191:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exit  files.   Finally,  in  subsection  D  we  examine  how  contacts  and  interactions  between
19:691:56289:19:34:70:456:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents and children in complex families are related to end-of-life transfers.
19:692:56367:34:26:70:466:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A. Evidence from Fixed Effects and Instrumental Variables Models
19:693:56431:26:18:70:523:662:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:FE Estimates— As mentioned in Section 3, the RE estimates presented so far rely on the
19:694:56517:18:18:70:524:644:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumption that the unobserved individual-specific component of the error term and our
19:695:56603:18:18:70:524:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measure of family complexity (i.e.,νiandCit, respectively, in equation (1)) are uncorre-
19:696:56691:18:18:70:524:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lated.  A concern with the RE estimates is that the effect of family complexity on bequest
19:697:56781:18:18:70:524:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:behavior  might  be  spurious.   But  this  may  be  due  precisely  to  the  mutual  association
19:698:56878:18:18:70:524:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that family complexity and bequest behavior share with some unmeasured causal factor.
19:699:56963:18:19:70:524:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For instance, the association between having stepchildren (or having no contact with ge-
19:700:57051:19:18:70:524:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:netic children) and not mentioning all children equally in the will may not be driven by
19:701:57139:18:18:70:524:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:family complexity per se.  Rather, it may reflect some hard-to-measure characteristics of
19:702:57228:18:18:70:524:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the complex families in which older individuals live, such as the personality of their new
19:703:57318:18:18:70:190:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:partners or frail health.
19:704:57343:18:18:88:524:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although the primary goal of this paper is not to provide estimates that have a causal
19:705:57429:18:18:70:524:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interpretation,  we  also  performed  our  analysis  estimating  equation  (1)  with  FE  linear
19:706:57525:18:18:70:524:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability models.  Indeed we do not see these estimates as offering a casual effect of
19:707:57613:18:18:70:524:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:family complexity,  but rather as providing us with a robustness check of the estimates
19:708:57700:18:18:70:524:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we reported earlier.  The FE estimates are shown in panel A of Table 7 where, for ease
19:709:57786:18:18:70:524:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  comparison,  we  also  report  the  RE  estimates  from  our  basic  specification  discussed
19:710:57883:18:18:70:111:355:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:above.29
19:711:57891:18:18:88:524:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Consider first the estimates for stepparents.  In the cases of inclusion of all children
19:712:57979:18:18:70:524:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the will and of equal division (columns (b) and (c) respectively), the FE estimates are
19:713:58069:18:18:70:524:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:just slightly smaller (in absolute value) than the corresponding benchmark RE estimates,
19:714:58157:18:18:70:524:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but they have the same sign and the same level of statistical significance.  The economic
19:715:58246:18:18:70:490:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interpretation of them is therefore the same as that of our previous RE estimates.
19:716:58328:18:18:88:524:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:If instead we look at the probability of having no will (column (a)), the FE estimates
19:717:58414:18:19:70:524:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reveal that stepparents are 2 percentage points less likely to have no will than their coun-
19:718:58506:19:18:70:524:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terparts without stepchildren, while the RE estimates revealed no difference between the
19:719:58594:18:18:70:524:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two groups of parents.  Albeit quantitatively small, this difference reveals that steppar-
19:720:58684:18:18:70:524:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ents may be less willing to rely on the default rules of heirship, than what we would have
19:721:58774:18:18:70:218:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inferred from the RE results.
19:722:58803:18:18:88:524:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Turning to no-contact families, the FE estimates show no significant relationship be-
19:723:58888:18:18:70:524:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tween  this  type  of  families  and  their  likelihood  of  having  no  will  (column  (d)).   The
19:724:58987:18:18:70:524:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference between the FE results and the RE estimates disappears,  however,  when we
19:725:59072:18:0:80:455:84:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:29The FE estimates from the other specifications are available in the online appendix.
20:726:59160:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:move to richer specifications: indeed Table 4 (specifications (c)–(e)) reveals no correlation
20:727:59253:18:19:70:383:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:among all groups of no-contact families, except for widowers.
20:728:59314:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, in the cases of inclusion of all children and of equal division, the FE estimates
20:729:59404:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confirm the negative link found with the RE models, but the FE estimates are about 70 to
20:730:59492:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:76 percent lower in absolute value.  This may suggest that the strength of the association
20:731:59582:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between  lack  of  contact  and  bequest  behavior  is  lower  than  that  suggested  by  the  RE
20:732:59679:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates.  But it may also reveal the presence of substantial measurement errors in the
20:733:59767:18:18:70:523:632:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:Citvariable which would bias our estimates toward zero.  Because of this possibility, we
20:734:59855:18:30:70:322:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:now turn to the instrumental variables approach.
20:735:59903:30:18:70:524:584:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:IV Estimates— To account for the potential endogeneity of family complexity in (1) and
20:736:59989:18:18:70:524:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:limit the possible problem of measurement error inCit, which could be exacerbated by
20:737:60073:18:18:70:524:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the FE model, we resort to an instrumental variables approach.  The variable we use to
20:738:60159:18:18:70:524:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instrument for family complexity is a novel measure of optimism, which we construct using
20:739:60248:18:18:70:524:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individual expectations information contained in the HRS questionnaires.  In particular,
20:740:60336:18:18:70:524:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we  use  a  measure  that  combines  the  individuals’  responses  to  two  questions,  one  on
20:741:60431:18:18:70:524:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inflation expectations over the next 10 years and the other on the expectation of a major
20:742:60520:18:18:70:524:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depression over the next 10 years.  We use optimism as a predictor of life choices which,
20:743:60609:18:18:70:524:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in turn, are linked to family complexity.  A complete description of this variable and its
20:744:60699:18:18:70:524:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subcomponents is available in the online appendix, where we also discuss its relationship
20:745:60788:18:19:70:403:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with individuals’ demographic and socioeconomic characteristics.
20:746:60852:19:18:88:524:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The only other economic study that correlates optimism to life choices (and remarriage,
20:747:60939:18:18:70:524:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:among others) is Puri and Robinson (2007).  Their measure of optimism, however, is based
20:748:61027:18:18:70:524:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on individuals’ life expectancy miscalibration (that is, the gap between individuals’ self-
20:749:61118:18:18:70:524:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reported life expectancy and that implied by actuarial tables), while ours does not refer
20:750:61207:18:18:70:524:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  events  that  are  affected  by  respondents’  life  decisions.   This  difference  is  important
20:751:61308:18:18:70:524:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because  life  expectancy  and  life  expectancy  miscalibration  are  likely  to  be  endogenous
20:752:61405:18:18:70:524:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to family structure and other life decisions, e.g., health choices, which in turn might be
20:753:61495:18:18:70:297:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:associated with individual bequest behavior.
20:754:61539:18:18:88:524:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Social and medical scientists have provided a wealth of evidence indicating that dispo-
20:755:61626:18:18:70:524:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sitional optimism — whereby one has a positive general outlook about future events and
20:756:61712:18:18:70:524:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:life in general — does matter for physical and psychological well-being (Scheier, Carver,
20:757:61801:18:18:70:524:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Bridges 1994; Solberg Nes and Segerstrom 2006).  For example, there is a large body
20:758:61888:18:18:70:524:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of evidence that documents that optimistic cancer patients face lower mortality risk and
20:759:61976:18:18:70:524:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experience faster recovery after surgery than pessimists (e.g., Schulz et al.  1996; Scheier
20:760:62068:18:18:70:524:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al.  1989; Rasmussen, Scheier, and Greenhouse 2009).  Puri and Robinson (2007) find
20:761:62154:18:18:70:524:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that more optimistic people work harder, expect to retire later, invest more in individual
20:762:62244:18:19:70:524:97:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stocks, and save more.  They also find that optimists who report they have been divorced
20:763:62332:19:0:70:242:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:before are more likely to remarry.
21:764:62368:0:18:88:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our IV results are reported in panel B of Table 7.  These are obtained from bivariate
21:765:62453:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probit regressions in which the first and second stages are estimated jointly. The first stage
21:766:62547:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predicts family complexity,Cit,  using the residuals of our measure of optimism from a
21:767:62633:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regression of optimism on age and sex.  To account for the fact that we include a predicted
21:768:62724:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variable, the bivariate probit standard errors are estimated using a bootstrap method that,
21:769:62815:18:18:70:484:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:due to the panel nature of the data, also allows for within-individual correlation.
21:770:62898:18:18:88:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Irrespective of the type of complex family (whether stepfamily or no-contact family)
21:771:62982:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  across  all  three  bequest  outcomes,  theχ2tests  and  correspondingp-values  in  the
21:772:63074:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first stage suggest that our instrument is always statistically relevant.  We find that, on
21:773:63165:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average, an increase in optimism of 1 percent leads to a reduction in the likelihood that
21:774:63254:18:18:70:463:578:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:the HRS respondents live in a complex family of 0.1–0.2 percentage points.30
21:775:63330:18:18:88:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  second  stage  estimates  indicate  that  stepparents  are  26  percentage  points  less
21:776:63423:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to include all children in their wills and 31 percentage points less likely to intend
21:777:63515:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equal division of their estate than parents with only genetic children (columns (b) and (c),
21:778:63607:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:respectively).  These are very close to the benchmark RE estimates we found in Section 4.
21:779:63696:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The corresponding IV estimates for the sample of parents without contact with at least
21:780:63782:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one of their genetic children are instead significantly larger in absolute value than those
21:781:63873:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtained from the RE models (columns (e) and (f)).  This last result suggests the possible
21:782:63963:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:presence  of  unobserved  common  factors  shared  by  the  processes  that  generate  bequest
21:783:64057:19:18:70:369:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intentions and the likelihood of living in a complex family.
21:784:64117:18:18:88:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, the IV estimates in columns (a) and (d) show that parents in complex fam-
21:785:64199:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ilies are, respectively, 21 and 6 percentage points more likely to have no will than their
21:786:64289:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple family counterparts.  The latter estimate is statistically insignificant and is indis-
21:787:64382:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinguishable from the corresponding RE estimate shown in Table 4.  The significant and
21:788:64468:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:positive sign of the former coefficient, instead, may indicate that parents in stepfamilies
21:789:64559:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are substantially more reluctant to make wills than implied by the RE models in Table
21:790:64644:18:30:70:367:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:3.  Family complexity may encourage this procrastination.
21:791:64701:30:18:88:524:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, the results presented in Section 4 provide us with a useful benchmark, with
21:792:64784:18:18:70:524:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the RE estimates being almost always between the FE estimates and the IV estimates.
21:793:64867:18:18:70:524:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Although the FE model does not impose a zero-correlation assumption between the unob-
21:794:64952:18:18:70:524:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:served individual component of the residuals andCit, its estimates might exacerbate the
21:795:65039:18:17:70:524:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:problems due to measurement error in the family complexity variables.  The gaps between
21:796:65126:17:16:80:524:170:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:30This result is not in line with the finding by Puri and Robinson (2007) that more optimistic people
21:797:65227:16:12:70:524:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:are more likely to remarry.  A number of reasons may explain this difference.  For example, we employ a
21:798:65330:12:12:70:524:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:different measure of optimism.  Moreover, the individuals in their sample are almost twenty years younger
21:799:65435:12:12:70:524:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:than the HRS respondents in our study.  Finally, we consider the whole population while they focus on
21:800:65536:12:12:70:524:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:individuals who have been divorced.  For comparison, we also repeated our analysis on the subsample of
21:801:65638:12:12:70:524:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:divorced individuals.  We found results similar to those shown in Table 7.  These estimates are available in
21:802:65746:12:12:70:524:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the online appendix.  More generally, our findings are consistent with the evidence from the psychological
21:803:65852:12:12:70:524:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:literature that documents that optimists are a positive resource for close relationships (Srivastava et al.
21:804:65959:12:0:70:182:70:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:2006; Carver et al.  2010).
22:805:65988:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the IV and the RE estimates shown in Table 7 might instead reflect the downward bias
22:806:66072:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the RE estimates attributable to measurement errors, with only a small bias in the RE
22:807:66160:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates induced by omitted variables.31They might also reflect unobserved differences
22:808:66247:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between  the  characteristics  of  the  treatment  and  comparison  groups  (optimists  versus
22:809:66341:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pessimists in our case) implicit in the IV approach.  Our results therefore suggest that the
22:810:66433:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RE estimates are likely to be not far off the mark.  For this reason the results we report
22:811:66523:18:34:70:345:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the following subsections rely on RE specifications.
22:812:66578:34:26:70:284:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:B. Transitions in Bequest Intentions
22:813:66614:26:18:70:524:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Exploiting the longitudinal aspect of the HRS, we analyzechangesin bequest intentions.
22:814:66700:18:18:70:524:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For each of our three bequest outcomes,  these can be readily estimated using equation
22:815:66786:18:18:70:524:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1) conditional onYi,t−1= 0 orYi,t−1= 1.  Individuals have a high degree of persistence
22:816:66873:18:18:70:524:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  their  intentions.   Of  those  who  do  not  have  a  will  in  one  wave  88  percent  remain
22:817:66972:18:18:70:524:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:without a will in the subsequent wave, and 86 percent (or 79 percent) of those intending
22:818:67060:18:18:70:524:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to bequeath to all children (or to all children equally) at one point in time continue to do
22:819:67152:18:18:70:298:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so the subsequent time they are interviewed.
22:820:67196:18:18:88:524:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  focus  on  the  transitions  from  not  having  a  will  to  having  a  will,  from  having
22:821:67291:18:18:70:524:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a will that does not include all children to having a will that includes all children, and
22:822:67381:18:19:70:524:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from unequal intended bequests to equal intended bequests.32In our analysis we explicitly
22:823:67470:19:18:70:524:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consider the interaction of the presence of stepchildren or parental absence with changes in
22:824:67562:18:18:70:524:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents’ marital status (e.g., divorce and death of a spouse).  Several other changes might
22:825:67653:18:18:70:524:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interact with bequest plans and the joint presence of genetic children and stepchildren or
22:826:67743:18:18:70:524:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the lack of contact with genetic children, such as changes in parental health and changes
22:827:67832:18:18:70:524:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in children’s economic situations.  These however are not modeled, due to the small size
22:828:67920:18:18:70:147:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of our samples.
22:829:67935:18:18:88:524:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 8 shows the results from a specification that includes changes in our basic set
22:830:68020:18:18:70:524:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of controls, health status, money transfers to children, and parental income and wealth
22:831:68107:18:18:70:524:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(comparable to specification (d) in Tables 3–6).  The estimates of interest are robust to
22:832:68196:18:18:70:524:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their exclusion. In panel A we look at stepparents, while in panel B we focus on no-contact
22:833:68287:18:18:70:524:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents.  For each transition, we report two sets of coefficients.  In the first column, we
22:834:68378:18:18:70:524:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:present the impact of having stepchildren or genetic children with whom the parent has no
22:835:68467:18:18:70:524:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact on the transition under study.  In the second we also show the interaction terms of
22:836:68558:18:17:70:524:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the stepparent or no-contact parent variable with two changes in parental marital status:
22:837:68647:17:16:80:524:158:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:31This is confirmed by positive regression coefficients found when we regress each measure of family
22:838:68747:16:12:70:524:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:complexity,Cit, on the random effectsνifor each bequest outcome,Yit.  See Card (2001) for a similar
22:839:68846:12:8:70:389:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:interpretation in the context of the estimation of the return to schooling.
22:840:68921:8:16:80:524:122:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:32The  picture  emerging  from  the  three  transitions  in  the  opposite  directions  is  consistent  with  that
22:841:69035:16:12:70:524:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:obtained from the three transitions just mentioned.  They are therefore not presented, but are available
22:842:69139:12:12:70:524:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:in the web appendix.  In the same appendix, for completeness, we also report the estimates obtained from
22:843:69243:12:12:70:524:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:all other transitions, such as from not having a will to having a will that includes all children equally, or
22:844:69352:12:0:70:353:70:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:from having a will that includes all children to not having a will.
23:845:69421:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from marriage to divorce and from marriage to widowhood.  This is important because,
23:846:69505:18:19:70:480:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following divorce or the death of a spouse, an individual might write a new will.
23:847:69586:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In panels C and D we analyze this possibility more directly by considering only the
23:848:69669:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subsample of widows and widowers.  In this case, we first analyze whether parents write
23:849:69756:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a new will or change an old will after the death of their partner (first column).  In the
23:850:69845:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:second column we present the estimates of how the presence of stepchildren or no-contact
23:851:69933:18:18:70:302:650:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:children changes bequest intentions further.33
23:852:69979:18:18:88:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Panel A of Table 8 reveals that the transition from not having a will to having a will
23:853:70065:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  not  affected  by  the  joint  presence  of  stepchildren  and  genetic  children.   This  is  also
23:854:70168:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case when the presence of stepchildren is interacted with the two changes in marital
23:855:70256:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:status.   The  joint  presence  of  genetic  children  and  stepchildren,  instead,  significantly
23:856:70354:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduces  the  probability  of  a  transition  to  a  will  in  which  all  children  are  included  as
23:857:70456:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well as the transition from unequal to equal bequests.  Having stepchildren reduces the
23:858:70543:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:former transition by almost 9 percentage points (column (c)) and the latter by around 8
23:859:70630:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points (column (e)).  Controlling for changes in parents’ marital status does
23:860:70718:18:18:70:383:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not significantly alter these results (see columns (d) and (f)).
23:861:70782:18:18:88:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The presence of stepchildren therefore is negatively correlated not only with the prob-
23:862:70869:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ability of equal intended bequests but also with the probability of changing the will from
23:863:70959:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unequal to equal treatment of children.  Having lost a partner through divorce or death
23:864:71046:19:18:70:309:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generally makes this transition even less likely.
23:865:71095:18:18:88:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Panel  B  confirms  virtually  all  the  previous  results  for  the  case  of  parents  with  no-
23:866:71193:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact children.  Generally the estimated effects are larger in absolute value among these
23:867:71284:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents than among stepparents.  The only exceptions are in columns (d) and (f) where
23:868:71369:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the reductions in the probability that no-contact children are included in the will and are
23:869:71460:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mentioned equally are not statistically significant if the no-contact parent’s partner dies.
23:870:71552:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This could be driven by the low statistical power of our small samples.  We assess this
23:871:71639:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:issue more directly in the next two panels in which we focus on the subsample of widows
23:872:71726:18:18:70:142:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and widowers.
23:873:71739:18:18:88:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For this subsample we draw attention to four interesting results.  First, the estimates
23:874:71826:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for widowed stepparents are qualitatively similar to those for no-contact parents.  Second,
23:875:71917:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:widowhood in all complex families increases the likelihood of changing bequest intentions:
23:876:72007:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it increases the transition to writing a will, having a will in which all children are men-
23:877:72098:18:18:70:524:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tioned,  and  having  a  will  in  which  all  children  are  equally  included  (columns  (a),  (c),
23:878:72199:18:18:70:524:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  (e)).   Third,  stepchildren  or  no-contact  children  neither  increase  nor  decrease  par-
23:879:72298:18:18:70:524:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ents’ greater propensity of writing a will (column (b)), but offset their parents’ greater
23:880:72388:18:18:70:524:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:propensities of including all children in the wills and including them all equally (columns
23:881:72479:18:19:70:524:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(d)  and  (f)).   Fourth,  the  presence  of  stepchildren  combined  with  the  loss  of  a  spouse
23:882:72579:19:16:80:524:90:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:33Other interesting changes in marital status (e.g., remarriage and repartnering) cannot be analyzed
23:883:72679:16:0:70:250:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:separately due to sample size limitations.
24:884:72723:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:further  reduces  the  likelihood  of  moving  to  a  will  with  full  inclusion  by  13  percentage
24:885:72824:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points and the likelihood of moving to a will with equal division by 9 percentage points
24:886:72912:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(panel C). Such further reductions are not observed among no-contact parents (panel D).
24:887:72999:18:34:70:428:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This evidence is consistent with what we found in the top two panels.
24:888:73068:34:26:70:435:670:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:C. Actual End-of-Life Transfers:  Evidence from the Exit Files
24:889:73130:26:18:70:524:644:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The HRS exit files provide direct information about end-of-life transfers.  The exit files
24:890:73220:18:18:70:524:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contain reports by the surviving spouse or partner or by other close family members of
24:891:73306:18:18:70:524:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the deceased HRS respondent and they allow us to analyze the actual division of estates
24:892:73393:18:18:70:524:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rather than bequest intentions.  Unlike the core files, the exit files do not suffer from right
24:893:73488:18:18:70:524:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:censoring but they are much smaller than the core files and the HRS respondents who die
24:894:73575:18:19:70:354:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:early are not a random subsample of HRS respondents.
24:895:73627:19:18:88:524:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 9 gives a summary of our results.  For each outcome we show probit estimates
24:896:73709:18:18:70:524:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from two specifications.  The first includes controls for standard demographics (column
24:897:73796:18:18:70:524:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(a)),  while  the  second  further  controls  for  year-of-death  fixed  effects,  an  indicator  for
24:898:73897:18:18:70:524:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whether the death was expected, earlier transfers to children, and parental wealth (column
24:899:73987:18:18:70:102:463:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:(b)).34
24:900:73994:18:18:88:524:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When looking at the probability of intestate succession (in the first two columns of
24:901:74078:18:18:70:524:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Table 9), the estimated coefficient of the stepchild variable is always statistically indis-
24:902:74170:18:18:70:524:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinguishable from 0.  This result, which holds true across all family types and for both
24:903:74258:18:18:70:524:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fathers  and  mothers,  confirms  the  general  findings  reported  in  Table  3.   From  the  exit
24:904:74357:18:18:70:524:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:files, however, we detect neither the negative effect for widows nor the positive effect for
24:905:74449:18:18:70:524:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:divorced fathers which were found using the core files.  This might reflect an actual change
24:906:74541:18:18:70:524:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in parents’ behavior with respect to their bequest intentions.  That is, it is possible that
24:907:74633:18:18:70:524:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:widows and divorced fathers with stepchildren are not more (nor less) likely to rely on
24:908:74720:18:18:70:524:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intestacy law than their counterparts without stepchildren.  But it could also be due to
24:909:74808:18:18:70:448:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the low statistical power implied by the small sample size of the exit files.
24:910:74885:18:18:88:524:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the next two columns, we consider the probability of including all children in the
24:911:74970:18:18:70:524:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will.   This  is  estimated  on  the  subsample  of  HRS  respondents  who  wrote  a  will,  while
24:912:75068:18:19:70:524:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those  who  died  intestate  are  not  included.   We  generally  find  that  having  stepchildren
24:913:75166:19:18:70:524:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does  not  affect  the  likelihood  that  all  children  are  included  (column  (a)).   This  result
24:914:75267:18:18:70:524:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:emerges for the full sample as well as for all the subsamples of mothers and fathers by
24:915:75354:18:18:70:524:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marital status.  It contradicts what we found in Table 5 using the core files.  Indeed, in
24:916:75444:18:18:70:524:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two out of the nine cases under specification (b), we even find apositiveand significant
24:917:75532:18:18:70:524:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of the stepparent indicator.  This result might indicate a strategy according to which
24:918:75625:18:18:70:524:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepparents end up including all their children (including stepchildren) in their final will.
24:919:75718:18:16:80:524:102:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:34The table reports the estimates on the stepchild indicator found among families with stepparents.
24:920:75817:16:12:70:524:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:The exit files do not allow us to perform the same analysis on parents who did not have contacts with
24:921:75918:12:0:70:165:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:their genetic children.
25:922:75943:0:18:88:523:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Would all children be includedequally?  The last two columns, where we present the
25:923:76025:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates  for  the  probability  of  equal  bequests,  suggest  that  they  are  not.35In  fact,
25:924:76122:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  line  with  the  bequest  intention  estimates  of  Table  6,  the  results  in  Table  9  indicate
25:925:76225:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the presence of stepchildren reduces the probability that actual bequests are equal
25:926:76313:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by  9  percentage  points  (first  line,  specification  (a)).   This  impact  is  roughly  a  fourth
25:927:76414:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the magnitude of the corresponding impact on intended bequests.  As in the case of
25:928:76499:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  core  files,  the  estimated  effect  of  stepchildren  on  equal  actual  bequests  is  greater
25:929:76600:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  fathers  than  for  mothers,  although  the  relatively  large  standard  errors  make  this
25:930:76697:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differential  response  by  gender  statistically  indistinguishable  from  0.   We  also  cannot
25:931:76794:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:detect differential impacts for the subpopulations of parents who experienced divorce or
25:932:76882:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the death of a spouse or partner.  But the probability of equal bequests is particularly
25:933:76970:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low for divorced mothers and widowers, with estimated effects similar to those we found
25:934:77057:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the intended bequests.  Some of these effects lose their statistical significance when we
25:935:77150:18:18:70:502:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimate specification (b), but by and large the main pattern of results is confirmed.
25:936:77236:18:18:88:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, the presence of stepchildren does not affect the probability of writing a will.
25:937:77323:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stepparents might explicitly decide to rely on intestacy statutes which would leave nothing
25:938:77414:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to stepchildren.  For parents who die with a will, the actual bequests observed in the exit
25:939:77505:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:files are largely consistent with the bequest intentions reported in the core files.  Unequal
25:940:77598:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bequests  are  a  distinguishing  feature  of  stepparents  whose  genetic  children  are  favored
25:941:77696:19:34:70:324:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over stepchildren in the actual division of estates.
25:942:77748:34:26:70:342:381:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:D. Interactions between Parents and Children
25:943:77792:26:18:70:524:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now focus on how interactions between parents and children are related to the proba-
25:944:77879:18:18:70:524:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bility that the children are mentioned in the will.  We first look at the stepparent–stepchild
25:945:77973:18:18:70:524:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interaction and investigate whether stepchildren are less likely to be included in the will
25:946:78064:18:18:70:387:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a stepparent when the stepparent also has genetic children.
25:947:78126:18:18:88:524:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 10 presents random effects probit estimates of the probability that a stepchild is
25:948:78214:18:18:70:524:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mentioned in the stepparent’s will for the whole sample of stepchildren.  The table shows
25:949:78303:18:18:70:524:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the results from five specifications.  In specification (a) we include a basic set of controls
25:950:78397:18:19:70:524:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e., parent and child’s age and gender), the age at which the child became a stepchild, and
25:951:78490:19:18:70:524:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the number of years spent with the stepparent.  Specification (b) also controls for whether
25:952:78581:18:18:70:524:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the stepparent reported providing care for the stepchild’s child(ren), while specification
25:953:78671:18:18:70:524:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(c) includes an indicator of whether the stepchild was the main recipient of inter vivos
25:954:78759:18:18:70:524:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers from the stepparent. Specification (d) adds a measure of the stepchild’s predicted
25:955:78851:18:18:70:524:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:income, which was constructed using the procedure described in Section 3, and controls
25:956:78937:18:18:70:524:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the within-family difference between the stepchild’s predicted income and the genetic
25:957:79026:18:18:70:524:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:child’s income (or the income mean when there are two or more genetic children).  We
25:958:79110:18:0:80:470:84:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:35As before, this analysis is based only on the subsample of parents who died with a will.
26:959:79202:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distinguish three subgroups, one in which the stepchild’s income is equal or greater than
26:960:79291:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the genetic child’s, another in which it is 1–49 percent lower, and the last one in which
26:961:79380:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it is 50+ percent lower.36Finally, specification (e) includes an indicator of whether the
26:962:79469:18:18:70:433:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepparent expects to receive help from his/her stepchild in the future.
26:963:79541:18:18:88:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 10 reveals that for a child whose stepparent also has a genetic child the prob-
26:964:79626:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ability of being included in the will is 3–4 percentage points lower, an average impact of
26:965:79716:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about 15 percent (columns (a)–(e)).  This is consistent with the genetic-child hypothesis
26:966:79805:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:according to which parents tend to favor children who share their genes.  This negative
26:967:79892:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relationship is entirely eliminated,  however,  if the stepchild’s predicted income is lower
26:968:79984:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than the genetic child’s (specification (d)).  Nearly two-fifths of stepchildren in the sample
26:969:80078:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have relatively lower incomes.  This finding is consistent with altruism if parents not only
26:970:80170:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are more likely to mention low-income stepchildren in their wills (as we find here), but
26:971:80258:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also  give  them  more.   We  cannot  test  this  last  point  because,  as  mentioned  in  Section
26:972:80357:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:3.B,  the  HRS  does  not  contain  any  information  about  the  monetary  amount  that  the
26:973:80450:18:18:70:304:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:respondents intend to bequeath to each child.
26:974:80495:18:18:88:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Across all specifications, the older the stepparent the higher the likelihood that the
26:975:80581:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchild is included in the will: the stepchild penalty is offset if the stepparent is 10 years
26:976:80677:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:older than the average stepparent.  This may indicate a greater need for the stepchild’s
26:977:80765:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assistance.  These findings mirror the relationship between parents and their genetic chil-
26:978:80856:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren.  In particular, they suggest that stepparents may use bequests to elicit a long-term
26:979:80946:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:flow of reciprocal services rather than episodic short-term care.  It is possible, in fact, that
26:980:81042:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:episodic short-term care could be “paid for” by inter vivos transfers.  This behavior is con-
26:981:81135:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sistent with the strategic use of bequests postulated by Bernheim, Shleifer and Summers
26:982:81222:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1985).  Children whose stepparents are in poor/fair health (another possible indicator of
26:983:81312:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:need) have however a 5–6 percentage pointdecreasein the probability of being included
26:984:81397:18:18:70:125:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the will.
26:985:81409:18:18:88:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Table 10 also shows that, regardless of the age at which a child acquired the stepparent,
26:986:81498:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the more years he/she spent with the stepparent the higher the likelihood of being in-
26:987:81584:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cluded in the will: 7–10 years of stepchildhood completely eliminate the stepchild penalty.
26:988:81675:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, a stepchild’s probability of inclusion in the will goes up by about 6–8 percent-
26:989:81765:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age  points  if  the  stepparent  reports  having  provided  care  for  the  stepchild’s  child(ren)
26:990:81865:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(specifications  (b)–(e))  and  by  another  13–14  percentage  points  if  the  stepchild  is  also
26:991:81965:18:18:70:524:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the main recipient of inter vivos transfers (specifications (c)–(e)).  This may reflect trust
26:992:82058:18:18:70:524:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and bonding, which are strengthened by repeated interactions over longer time periods.
26:993:82144:18:18:70:524:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, if stepparents expect help from their stepchildren in the future, the likelihood the
26:994:82237:18:19:70:524:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchild is mentioned in the will goes up by 14 percentage points (a 54 percent increase
26:995:82326:19:16:80:524:108:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:36We checked the sensitivity of this cutoff using different partitions (e.g., at one-third and two-thirds
26:996:82431:16:11:70:524:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of the genetic child’s income), and found results that are essentially identical to those shown in Table 10.
26:997:82539:11:0:70:288:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:These alternative estimates are thus not reported.
27:998:82591:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over the baseline probability).  This result suggests again the presence of exchange motives
27:999:82683:18:19:70:386:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with parents using bequests strategically toward stepchildren.
27:1000:82745:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Stratifying  the  sample  by  gender  (see  Appendix  Tables  A5  and  A6),  we  find  that
27:1001:82836:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the negative association between the probability of being mentioned in the will and the
27:1002:82923:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:presence of a step-sibling (i.e., the variable ‘stepparent has own genetic children’) is con-
27:1003:83016:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:centrated  among  male  stepchildren,  who  experience  a  reduction  in  this  probability  of
27:1004:83111:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about  5–9  percentage points.  Female stepchildren experience  a reduction of  at most 3
27:1005:83200:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points but this reduction is never statistically significant.  For female stepchil-
27:1006:83294:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren  the  probability  of  being  mentioned  in  the  will  is  also  unaffected  by  differences  in
27:1007:83396:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children’s predicted incomes.  The relationship between stepparental expectation about
27:1008:83482:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:future  help  and  inclusion  in  the  will  is  stronger  for  female  stepchildren  (17  percentage
27:1009:83583:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points for female as opposed to 11 percentage points for male stepchildren).  The same
27:1010:83669:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pattern of results, with the same gender differences, persists when we focus on the sub-
27:1011:83757:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:samples of stepchildren of divorced and widowed parents.  These results are reported in
27:1012:83844:18:18:70:175:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the online appendix.
27:1013:83864:18:18:88:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We now turn our attention to no-contact parent–genetic child interactions and inves-
27:1014:83948:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tigate how contacts in complex families affect bequest intentions.  In Table 11 we report
27:1015:84037:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:how the probability that a genetic child is mentioned in his/her parent’s will varies with
27:1016:84127:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  frequency  of  contact  and  with  the  fact  that  the  parent’s  spouse  is  not  genetically
27:1017:84227:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related to the child.37The first two columns of the table show that parents who have
27:1018:84311:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no contact with their genetic children are 21–24 percentage points less likely to mention
27:1019:84400:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:them in their wills.  The lack of parent–child contact therefore more than halves the child’s
27:1020:84493:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:odds of inclusion in the parent’s will.  Having infrequent rather than frequent contacts also
27:1021:84586:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduces the likelihood of inclusion by 14–15 percentage points, but, as indicated by the
27:1022:84674:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:p-values at the bottom of the table, the difference between having infrequent contacts and
27:1023:84764:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:having no contact is always statistically significant.  These results do not change when we
27:1024:84855:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:add controls for child’s income and other parent-child interaction terms (e.g., grandchild’s
27:1025:84947:18:18:70:227:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:care and inter vivos transfers).
27:1026:84979:18:18:88:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We find that the “no-contact genetic child penalty” is fully offset if the child is the main
27:1027:85071:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recipient of inter vivos transfers.  This might reflect earlier (more frequent) interactions.
27:1028:85164:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Similarly,  if  the  no-contact  child  is  a  female,  her  penalty  is  reduced  by  60–90  percent,
27:1029:85266:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perhaps reflecting the flow of other services expected by the parent but not observed in
27:1030:85354:18:18:70:117:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the HRS.
27:1031:85362:18:18:88:524:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  columns  (c)  and  (d)  we  explore  how  the  child’s  odds  of  being  mentioned  in  the
27:1032:85457:18:18:70:524:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will  change  not  only  when  the  child  has  infrequent  or  no  contact  with  the  parent  but
27:1033:85556:18:19:70:524:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also if he/she is not the genetic child of the parent’s partner and if the parent expects
27:1034:85645:19:16:80:524:108:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:37Due  to  small  sample  size  we  could  not  estimate  a  specification  which  included  the  within-family
27:1035:85756:16:11:70:524:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:coefficient of variation in children’s income.  We thus cannot use the estimates in Table 11 to assess the
27:1036:85862:11:0:70:173:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:role played by altruism.
28:1037:85888:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to receive help from him/her in the future.  We find that, if the no-contact child is also
28:1038:85978:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetically  unrelated  to  the  parent’s  partner,  his/her  probability  of  being  included  in
28:1039:86076:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  will  is  further  reduced  by  8  percentage  points  (column  (c)).   This  means  that  for
28:1040:86175:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no-contact stepchildren the odds of inclusion are essentially reduced to zero.  As before,
28:1041:86265:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:being the main recipient of inter vivos transfers and being a female will reduce the penalty
28:1042:86357:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:substantially but will not eliminate it entirely.  Expecting help from the absent child in
28:1043:86447:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the future does not significantly affect the likelihood of mentioning him/her in the will
28:1044:86536:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(column (d)).  This suggests that parents do not anticipate receiving any help from genetic
28:1045:86627:18:18:70:326:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children with whom they have no regular contact.
28:1046:86675:18:18:88:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we explore how the lack of contact interacts with the absence of a relationship
28:1047:86763:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the parent’s partner as well as with the parent’s expectation of receiving help in the
28:1048:86854:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:future (column (e)).  If parents expect to receive help from their absent genetic children
28:1049:86944:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the future, the probability that such children are included in the will increases by 39
28:1050:87034:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percentage points.  This more than offsets the penalty of having no contact.  However, if
28:1051:87123:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the parent formed a new family and the absent child is not related to the parent’s new
28:1052:87209:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:partner/spouse,  the chances that the absent child is mentioned in the will are reduced
28:1053:87296:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by 28 percentage points, leading to an absent-child penalty of about 17 points, almost 40
28:1054:87385:18:18:70:248:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:percent of the baseline probability.
28:1055:87421:18:19:88:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We also conducted this analysis separately for male and female children, the results
28:1056:87505:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  which  are  shown  in  web  appendix.   These  estimates  broadly  confirm  the  results  in
28:1057:87601:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Table 11, with effects that are generally similar for sons and daughters.  However, women
28:1058:87690:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(but not men) who are not the genetic children of the parent’s partner face an additional
28:1059:87779:18:18:70:359:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:penalty only if they have no contacts with their parents.
28:1060:87836:18:18:88:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In sum, parents are more likely to transfer resources to children who share their genes
28:1061:87923:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than to stepchildren who are genetically unrelated to them.  But a simple evolutionary
28:1062:88009:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:story, such as the genetic-child hypothesis, does not explain what we observe in the data
28:1063:88098:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as, for example, in the case of no-contact parents.  Furthermore, bequests to stepchildren
28:1064:88188:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are affected by altruistic and exchange motives.  Parents are likely to leave bequests to
28:1065:88277:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their low-income stepchildren suggesting altruistic motives.  And stepchildren are more
28:1066:88364:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely to be mentioned in their stepparents’ wills if the stepparents are older suggesting
28:1067:88454:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exchange  motives.   Trust  and  bonding  seem  to  be  highly  relevant  within  all  complex
28:1068:88548:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:families:  there is no stepchild penalty if stepparents help with child care or have already
28:1069:88640:18:18:70:524:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:made other transfers.  Similar patterns occur between parents and their no-contact genetic
28:1070:88730:18:18:70:524:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children.  The relationship between stepchildren and parents in complex families requires
28:1071:88819:18:0:70:510:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deeper, more subtle explanations than those provided by the genetic-child hypothesis.
29:1072:88906:0:26:70:140:759:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6.  Theory
29:1073:88916:26:18:70:524:733:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here we provide a simple framework to interpret the results of the previous two sections.
29:1074:89005:18:18:70:524:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We borrow our key insights from the work by Behrman, Pollak and Taubman (1982, 1986,
29:1075:89089:18:18:70:101:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1995).
29:1076:89095:18:18:88:524:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Consider a family comprised of one older parent (e.g., the surviving spouse) and two
29:1077:89179:18:18:70:524:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children,  childgwho  is  her  genetic  child  and  childswho  is  her  stepchild.38Suppose
29:1078:89270:18:19:70:524:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the parent has a separable welfare function defined over expected bequests for each child,
29:1079:89360:19:18:70:524:624:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:W(Bg,Bs).  The parent maximizesWsubject to three constraints.  The first constraint is
29:1080:89446:18:18:70:524:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the budget constraint that applies to resources devoted to bequests.  Such resources are
29:1081:89534:18:18:70:524:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denoted byR, while investments are denoted byH.  Assume the parent faces a fixed price
29:1082:89620:18:18:70:524:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for investments and the price is identical for both children.  Normalizing the investment
29:1083:89709:18:18:70:355:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price to 1, we can write the constraint asHg+Hs≤R.
29:1084:89759:18:18:88:524:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  other  two  constrains  are  the  bequest  production  functions,  one  for  each  child.
29:1085:89853:18:18:70:523:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:One of the arguments of these functions is bequest-related investments,H, which include
29:1086:89940:18:18:70:524:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the full history of each child’s health and human capital investments as well as material
29:1087:90029:18:18:70:524:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:help  and  money  transfers  that  the  parents  have  made  over  their  children’s  lives  and
29:1088:90125:18:18:70:524:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that,  in  turn,  might  depend  on  child  attributes,  such  as  age  and  sex.   Child-specific
29:1089:90223:18:18:70:524:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:income  and  family  circumstances  are  also  determinants  of  such  investments.   Another
29:1090:90316:18:18:70:523:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:argument,  labeledP,  comprises  bequest-relevant  parental  characteristics,  such  as  age,
29:1091:90409:18:18:70:524:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sex,  marital  status,  health,  income,  and  wealth.   A  final  category,  labeledT,  includes
29:1092:90506:18:18:70:524:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables that determine the trust relationship between each child and the parent.  This
29:1093:90594:18:18:70:524:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:takes account of physical proximity, contact, and bonding between parent and child, and is
29:1094:90684:18:18:70:524:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:signaled by and shaped by repeated interactions and relative bargaining powers.  Putting
29:1095:90772:18:19:70:524:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:together these arguments leads us to a child-specific bequest production function of the
29:1096:90860:19:18:70:246:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formBk=B(Hk,Pk,Tk),k=g,s.
29:1097:90885:18:18:88:524:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Provided the constrained maximization faced by the parent has an interior solution,
29:1098:90968:18:26:70:466:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the first-order condition for parental bequest related investment for childkis
29:1099:91046:26:16:101:119:255:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:∂W
29:1100:91048:16:0:101:121:239:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂Bk
29:1101:91051:0:16:124:144:255:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂Bk
29:1102:91054:16:0:124:145:239:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂Hk
29:1103:91057:0:35:150:193:247:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f10:C:−λ= 0,
29:1104:91063:35:18:70:524:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereλis  the  Lagrange  multiplier  for  the  budget  constraint  that  applies  to  resources
29:1105:91158:18:18:70:524:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:devoted to bequest-related investments for the two children.  Expressing the first-order
29:1106:91246:18:27:70:224:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditions in ratio form yields
29:1107:91277:27:16:101:145:149:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂W/∂Bs
29:1108:91283:16:0:101:145:133:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂W/∂Bg
29:1109:91289:0:0:150:159:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:=
29:1110:91290:0:16:164:210:149:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂Bg/∂Hg
29:1111:91297:16:0:164:210:133:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:C:∂Bs/∂Hs
29:1112:91304:0:36:212:215:141:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:.
29:1113:91305:36:18:70:524:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This expression, which does not include the unobservableλ, corresponds to the standard
29:1114:91391:18:0:80:524:87:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:38Alternatively, childscould be seen as the genetic child with whom the older parent has no contact.
30:1115:91493:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tangency  condition  for  a  constrained  maximum,  i.e.,  the  slope  of  the  parental  welfare
30:1116:91590:18:19:70:524:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function  equals  the  slope  of  the  bequest  possibility  frontier  for  childsversus  childg.
30:1117:91687:19:18:70:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is illustrated by pointAin Figure 6.  In this figure,  we assume equal concern for
30:1118:91774:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both children, so the indifference curves are symmetrical around the 45 degree line from
30:1119:91862:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the origin.  If we also assume a symmetric bequest possibility frontier, these assumptions
30:1120:91952:18:18:70:308:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imply equal bequests in equilibrium,B∗g=B∗s.
30:1121:91996:18:18:88:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Because  in  the  previous  two  sections  we  found  strong  evidence  of  unequal  bequest
30:1122:92088:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intentions  that  favor  genetic  children  over  stepchildren,  we  consider  changes  in  the  as-
30:1123:92188:18:18:70:524:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sumptions underlying Figure 6.  A straightforward change is to allow for unequal concern.
30:1124:92277:18:18:70:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For instance, stepparents may expect stepchildren to care less efficiently for them, or may
30:1125:92368:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:anticipate that stepchildren can also rely on their nonresidental biological parents for help
30:1126:92461:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and support.  This case is illustrated in Figure 7, with parental preferences favoring the
30:1127:92551:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:child genetically linked to the parent, that is childg.  If the production possibility frontier
30:1128:92646:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remains symmetric, a parent with unequal concern favoring the genetic child will divide
30:1129:92733:18:18:70:331:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the estates unequally, in such a way thatB∗g> B∗s.
30:1130:92783:18:18:88:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another departure from the benchmark of Figure 6 is through a change in the produc-
30:1131:92866:18:18:70:524:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion possibility frontier, while keeping the assumption of equal concern.  Parents might
30:1132:92954:18:18:70:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have skewed bequest related investments in favor of their genetic children, or genetic chil-
30:1133:93046:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren might have greater bargaining power (emotional capital) toward their parents than
30:1134:93132:19:18:70:523:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchildren do.  PointE∗in Figure 8 illustrates this case.  Clearly, if parents also have
30:1135:93222:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unequal  concern  favoring  their  genetic  children,  then  the  bequest  division  between  the
30:1136:93319:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepchild and the genetic child could be even more unequal, as illustrated by pointE′in
30:1137:93406:18:18:70:122:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the figure.
30:1138:93417:18:18:88:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The results in subsection 5.D suggest that the situation is less unfavorable to stepchil-
30:1139:93506:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dren  if  there  is  greater  bonding  and  trust  between  them  and  their  stepparents  and  if
30:1140:93604:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stepparents have greater access to the stepchildren’s family-specific capital.  This bonding
30:1141:93696:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  trust  is  signaled  and  fostered  by  the  stepparent  providing  care  for  the  stepchild’s
30:1142:93796:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children or making direct transfers to the stepchild.  When this happens, the bequest pos-
30:1143:93886:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sibility frontier can shift and the household will reach the new equilibriumE′′in Figure
30:1144:93974:18:39:70:291:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:8 (under the assumption of equal concern).
30:1145:94016:39:26:70:167:196:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:7.  Conclusion
30:1146:94030:26:18:70:524:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In the last thirty years, American families have experienced massive changes:  a retreat
30:1147:94118:18:18:70:524:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from marriage,  increased divorce and remarriage,  and growth in cohabitation and non-
30:1148:94204:18:18:70:524:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marital childbearing.  Stepparents and no-contact parents in complex families may be less
30:1149:94293:18:18:70:524:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:motivated than parents in traditional families to provide resources to children with whom
30:1150:94382:18:18:70:524:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they do not share their genes or have not shared their homes.  And children in complex
30:1151:94468:18:0:70:524:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:families may be less willing than children in traditional families to assist disabled older
31:1152:94561:0:18:70:524:759:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parents, especially those with whom they have no genetic connection or only briefly shared
31:1153:94651:18:19:70:110:741:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a home.
31:1154:94658:19:18:88:524:722:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For  younger  cohorts,  nonmarital  fertility  of  cohabiting  couples  who  break  up  and
31:1155:94749:18:18:70:524:704:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:repartner  will  substantially  increase  the  prevalence  of  complex  families.   Those  in  the
31:1156:94847:18:18:70:524:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HRS cohort are older, and their complex families are generally a by-product of divorce
31:1157:94933:18:18:70:524:668:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and remarriage.  The implications for intergenerational transfers of these changes in family
31:1158:95025:18:18:70:524:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:structure  are  difficult  to  predict  because  complex  families  created  by  cohabitation  and
31:1159:95123:18:18:70:524:632:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonmarital  fertility  in  younger  cohorts  may  behave  differently  from  those  created  by
31:1160:95218:18:18:70:275:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:divorce and remarriage in older cohorts.
31:1161:95258:18:18:88:524:596:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  have  shown  that  bequests  are  much  more  unequal  now  than  in  the  recent  past
31:1162:95349:18:18:70:524:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and much more unequal than generally recognized.  In simple families (i.e., families with
31:1163:95438:18:18:70:524:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:neither stepchildren nor no-contact children), equal bequests are the dominant pattern.  In
31:1164:95529:18:18:70:524:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complex families, however, we find substantial inequality in both bequest intentions and
31:1165:95617:18:18:70:524:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:actual bequests.  We cannot assess the relative importance of genetic ties and contact by
31:1166:95706:18:18:70:524:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:studying simple families because in such families all of the children have the same genetic
31:1167:95797:18:18:70:524:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ties with their parents.  But the bequest patterns we find in complex families imply that
31:1168:95886:18:18:70:212:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact trumps genetic ties.
31:1169:95914:18:18:88:524:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The economics literature on end-of-life transfers assumes that individuals, or at least
31:1170:96001:18:19:70:524:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:older individuals, make wills.  We find instead that parents often fail to write wills and,
31:1171:96092:19:18:70:524:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:either by design or default,  rely on intestacy law to determine the distribution of their
31:1172:96182:18:18:70:524:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estates.  For parents with stepchildren, the effect of relying on intestacy law is to leave
31:1173:96273:18:18:70:524:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:everything to genetic and legally-adopted children and nothing to stepchildren.  For no-
31:1174:96361:18:18:70:524:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contact parents, the effect of relying on intestacy law is to treat contact and no-contact
31:1175:96451:18:18:70:524:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:genetic children equally.  If parents understand the most basic provisions of intestacy law,
31:1176:96543:18:18:70:524:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this finding is puzzling.  It implies that parents who have had no contact with some of
31:1177:96630:18:18:70:524:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their genetic children are more likely to treat all of their genetic children equally than
31:1178:96720:18:18:70:524:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are parents who have maintained contact with all of their genetic children.  We suspect
31:1179:96807:18:18:70:524:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the absence of wills reflects the disutility of making wills (and contemplating death)
31:1180:96898:18:18:70:524:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rather than preferences for the distribution mandated by intestacy law.  Unfortunately,
31:1181:96985:18:18:70:524:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HRS provides no evidence that speaks to this issue.  Regardless of parents’ motivations
31:1182:97072:18:18:70:524:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for not making wills, we have shown that focusing exclusively on bequest intentions (i.e.,
31:1183:97162:18:18:70:524:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on parents who make wills) provides an incomplete and misleading picture of end-of-life
31:1184:97249:18:0:70:117:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers.
32:1185:97261:0:355:148:447:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 1:  Unequal Bequest Intentions, by Parent’s Gender

34:1189:97507:0:77:115:479:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 5:  Trends in Intestacy Rates, by Parent’s Age and Family Type
